class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.amsterdam.nl">www<wbr />.amsterdam<wbr />.nl</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Amsterdam</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ər/: &#39;er&#39; in &#39;letter&#39;">ər</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span style="font-size:85%;">UK also</span> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ər/: &#39;er&#39; in &#39;letter&#39;">ər</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <small>Dutch:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[ɑmstərˈdɑm]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nl-Amsterdam.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cd/Nl-Amsterdam.ogg" class="internal" title="Nl-Amsterdam.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>) is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_of_the_Netherlands" title="Capital of the Netherlands">capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_of_the_Netherlands" title="List of municipalities of the Netherlands">most populous city</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, with a population of 866,737 within the city proper, 1,380,872 in the <a href="/wiki/City_Region_of_Amsterdam" title="City Region of Amsterdam">urban area</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cbs_statline_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbs_statline-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and 2,410,960 in the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_metropolitan_area" title="Amsterdam metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-osamsterdam2015_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osamsterdam2015-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Amsterdam is in the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Netherlands" title="Provinces of the Netherlands">province</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Holland" title="North Holland">North Holland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-R2040_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-R2040-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Amsterdam is colloquially referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Venice_of_the_North" title="Venice of the North">Venice of the North</a>" due to its large number of canals which are a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>.  
</p><p>Amsterdam's name derives from <i>Amstelredamme</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_Eleven_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica_Eleven-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> indicative of the city's origin around a dam in the river <a href="/wiki/Amstel" title="Amstel">Amstel</a>. Originating as a small fishing village in the late 12th century, Amsterdam became one of the most important ports in the world in the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Dutch Golden Age</a> of the 17th century and became the leading centre for finance and trade.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In the 19th and 20th centuries, the city expanded, and many new neighbourhoods and suburbs were planned and built. The 17th-century <a href="/wiki/Canals_of_Amsterdam" title="Canals of Amsterdam">canals of Amsterdam</a> and the 19–20th century <a href="/wiki/Stelling_van_Amsterdam" title="Stelling van Amsterdam">Defence Line of Amsterdam</a> are on the <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage List</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sloten,_Amsterdam" title="Sloten, Amsterdam">Sloten</a>, annexed in 1921 by the municipality of Amsterdam, is the oldest part of the city, dating to the 9th century.
</p><p>As the commercial capital of the Netherlands and one of the top financial centres in Europe, Amsterdam is considered an <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">alpha- world city</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network" title="Globalization and World Cities Research Network">Globalization and World Cities</a> (GaWC) study group. The city is also the cultural capital of the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Many large Dutch institutions have their headquarters there, including <a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">Philips</a>, <a href="/wiki/AkzoNobel" title="AkzoNobel">AkzoNobel</a>, <a href="/wiki/TomTom" title="TomTom">TomTom</a> and <a href="/wiki/ING_Group" title="ING Group">ING</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Also, many of the world's largest companies are based in Amsterdam or established their European headquarters in the city, such as leading technology companies <a href="/wiki/Uber" title="Uber">Uber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tesla,_Inc." title="Tesla, Inc.">Tesla</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, Amsterdam was ranked the second best city to live in by the <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a> (EIU)<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and 12th globally on quality of living for environment and infrastructure by Mercer.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The city was ranked 4th place globally as top tech hub in the Savills Tech Cities 2019 report (2nd in Europe),<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and 3rd in innovation by Australian innovation agency 2thinknow in their Innovation Cities Index 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Amsterdam" title="Port of Amsterdam">Port of Amsterdam</a> is the fifth largest in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-RPA_Stat15_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RPA_Stat15-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Famous Amsterdam residents include the diarist <a href="/wiki/Anne_Frank" title="Anne Frank">Anne Frank</a>, artists <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vincent_van_Gogh" title="Vincent van Gogh">Van Gogh</a>, and philosopher <a href="/wiki/Baruch_Spinoza" title="Baruch Spinoza">Baruch Spinoza</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">Amsterdam Stock Exchange</a> is the oldest stock exchange in the world. <a href="/wiki/List_of_tourist_attractions_in_Amsterdam" title="List of tourist attractions in Amsterdam">Amsterdam's main attractions</a> include its <a href="/wiki/Canals_of_Amsterdam" title="Canals of Amsterdam">historic canals</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rijksmuseum" title="Rijksmuseum">Rijksmuseum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Van_Gogh_Museum" title="Van Gogh Museum">Van Gogh Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Stedelijk_Museum_Amsterdam" title="Stedelijk Museum Amsterdam">Stedelijk Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Amsterdam" title="Hermitage Amsterdam">Hermitage Amsterdam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Concertgebouw" title="Concertgebouw">Concertgebouw</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Anne_Frank_House" title="Anne Frank House">Anne Frank House</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nederlands_Scheepvaartmuseum" title="Nederlands Scheepvaartmuseum">Scheepvaartmuseum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Museum" title="Amsterdam Museum">Amsterdam Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Heineken_Experience" title="Heineken Experience">Heineken Experience</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Palace_of_Amsterdam" title="Royal Palace of Amsterdam">Royal Palace of Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natura_Artis_Magistra" title="Natura Artis Magistra">Natura Artis Magistra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hortus_Botanicus_Amsterdam" class="mw-redirect" title="Hortus Botanicus Amsterdam">Hortus Botanicus Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/NEMO_(museum)" title="NEMO (museum)">NEMO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Red-light_district" title="Red-light district">red-light district</a> and many <a href="/wiki/Coffeeshop_(Netherlands)" title="Coffeeshop (Netherlands)">cannabis coffee shops</a>. They draw more than 5&#160;million international visitors annually.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The city is also well known for its nightlife and festival activity; several of its nightclubs (<a href="/wiki/Melkweg" title="Melkweg">Melkweg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paradiso_(Amsterdam)" title="Paradiso (Amsterdam)">Paradiso</a>) are among the world's most famous. It is also one of the world's most multicultural cities, with at least 177 nationalities represented.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also <a href="/wiki/Names_of_European_cities_in_different_languages:_A" class="mw-redirect" title="Names of European cities in different languages: A">Other names of Amsterdam</a></div>
<p>After the floods of 1170 and 1173, locals near the river Amstel built a bridge over the river and a dam across it, giving its name to the village: "Aemstelredamme". The earliest recorded use of that name is in a document dated 27 October 1275, which exempted inhabitants of the village from paying <a href="/wiki/Toll_bridge" title="Toll bridge">bridge tolls</a> to Count <a href="/wiki/Floris_V,_Count_of_Holland" title="Floris V, Count of Holland">Floris V</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBernsDaan199391_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBernsDaan199391-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMak199419_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMak199419-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> This allowed the inhabitants of the village of Aemstelredamme to travel freely through the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Holland" title="County of Holland">County of Holland</a>, paying no tolls at bridges, locks and dams. The certificate describes the inhabitants as <i>homines manentes apud Amestelledamme</i> (people residing near Amestelledamme).<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> By 1327, the name had developed into <i>Aemsterdam</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBernsDaan199391_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBernsDaan199391-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMak199418–20_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMak199418–20-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Amsterdam" title="History of Amsterdam">History of Amsterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Amsterdam" title="Timeline of Amsterdam">Timeline of Amsterdam</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding_and_Middle_Ages">Founding and Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Founding and Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_(6578772447).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Amsterdam_%286578772447%29.jpg/220px-Amsterdam_%286578772447%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Amsterdam_%286578772447%29.jpg/330px-Amsterdam_%286578772447%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Amsterdam_%286578772447%29.jpg/440px-Amsterdam_%286578772447%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_(6578772447).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Oude_Kerk,_Amsterdam" title="Oude Kerk, Amsterdam">Oude Kerk</a> was consecrated in 1306 CE.</div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam is much younger than Dutch cities such as <a href="/wiki/Nijmegen" title="Nijmegen">Nijmegen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Utrecht" title="Utrecht">Utrecht</a>. In October 2008, <a href="/wiki/Historical_geography" title="Historical geography">historical geographer</a> Chris de Bont suggested that the land around Amsterdam was being reclaimed as early as the late 10th century. This does not necessarily mean that there was already a settlement then, since <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">reclamation of land</a> may not have been for farming—it may have been for <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a>, for use as fuel.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Amsterdam was granted <a href="/wiki/City_rights_in_the_Low_Countries" title="City rights in the Low Countries">city rights</a> in either 1300 or 1306.<sup id="cite_ref-amnlgeschedenis_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amnlgeschedenis-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> From the 14th century on, Amsterdam flourished, largely from trade with the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a>. In 1345, an alleged <a href="/wiki/Blessed_Sacrament" title="Blessed Sacrament">Eucharistic miracle</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Kalverstraat" title="Kalverstraat">Kalverstraat</a> rendered the city an important place of pilgrimage until the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">adoption of the Protestant faith</a>. The Miracle devotion went underground but was kept alive. In the 19th century, especially after the jubilee of 1845, the devotion was revitalized and became an important national point of reference for Dutch Catholics. The <i><a href="/wiki/Stille_Omgang" title="Stille Omgang">Stille Omgang</a></i>—a silent walk or <a href="/wiki/Procession" title="Procession">procession</a> in civil attire—is the expression of the pilgrimage within the Protestant Netherlands since the late 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-stilleomgang_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stilleomgang-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> In the heyday of the Silent Walk, up to 90,000 pilgrims came to Amsterdam. In the 21st century this has reduced to about 5000.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conflict_with_Spain">Conflict with Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Conflict with Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bartholomeus_van_der_Helst,_Banquet_of_the_Amsterdam_Civic_Guard_in_Celebration_of_the_Peace_of_M%C3%BCnster.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Bartholomeus_van_der_Helst%2C_Banquet_of_the_Amsterdam_Civic_Guard_in_Celebration_of_the_Peace_of_M%C3%BCnster.jpg/330px-Bartholomeus_van_der_Helst%2C_Banquet_of_the_Amsterdam_Civic_Guard_in_Celebration_of_the_Peace_of_M%C3%BCnster.jpg" decoding="async" width="330" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Bartholomeus_van_der_Helst%2C_Banquet_of_the_Amsterdam_Civic_Guard_in_Celebration_of_the_Peace_of_M%C3%BCnster.jpg/495px-Bartholomeus_van_der_Helst%2C_Banquet_of_the_Amsterdam_Civic_Guard_in_Celebration_of_the_Peace_of_M%C3%BCnster.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Bartholomeus_van_der_Helst%2C_Banquet_of_the_Amsterdam_Civic_Guard_in_Celebration_of_the_Peace_of_M%C3%BCnster.jpg/660px-Bartholomeus_van_der_Helst%2C_Banquet_of_the_Amsterdam_Civic_Guard_in_Celebration_of_the_Peace_of_M%C3%BCnster.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4025" data-file-height="1705" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bartholomeus_van_der_Helst,_Banquet_of_the_Amsterdam_Civic_Guard_in_Celebration_of_the_Peace_of_M%C3%BCnster.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Amsterdam citizens celebrating the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_M%C3%BCnster" title="Peace of Münster">Peace of Münster</a>, 30 January 1648; painting by <a href="/wiki/Bartholomeus_van_der_Helst" title="Bartholomeus van der Helst">Bartholomeus van der Helst</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In the 16th century, the Dutch rebelled against <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II of Spain</a> and his successors. The main reasons for the uprising were the imposition of new taxes, the tenth penny, and the <a href="/wiki/Religious_persecution" title="Religious persecution">religious persecution</a> of Protestants by the newly introduced <a href="/wiki/Inquisition_of_the_Netherlands" title="Inquisition of the Netherlands">Inquisition</a>. The revolt escalated into the <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years&#39; War">Eighty Years' War</a>, which ultimately led to Dutch independence.<sup id="cite_ref-80yearswar_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80yearswar-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Strongly pushed by <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Revolt" title="Dutch Revolt">Dutch Revolt</a> leader <a href="/wiki/William_the_Silent" title="William the Silent">William the Silent</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a> became known for its relative <a href="/wiki/History_of_religion_in_the_Netherlands" title="History of religion in the Netherlands">religious</a> tolerance. <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Netherlands" title="History of the Jews in the Netherlands">Jews</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huguenot" class="mw-redirect" title="Huguenot">Huguenots</a> from France, prosperous merchants and printers from <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a>, and economic and religious refugees from the Spanish-controlled parts of the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a> found safety in Amsterdam. The influx of Flemish printers and the city's intellectual tolerance made Amsterdam a centre for the European <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">free press</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Centre_of_the_Dutch_Golden_Age">Centre of the Dutch Golden Age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Centre of the Dutch Golden Age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg/170px-Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg/255px-Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg/340px-Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1051" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Courtyard of the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">Amsterdam Stock Exchange</a> by <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_de_Witte" title="Emanuel de Witte">Emanuel de Witte</a>, 1653; the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">Amsterdam Stock Exchange</a> was the first <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> to introduce continuous trade in the early 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Braudel_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Braudel-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The 17th century is considered Amsterdam's <i><a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Golden Age</a></i>, during which it became the wealthiest city in the western world.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Ships sailed from Amsterdam to the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>, North America, and Africa, as well as present-day Indonesia, India, Sri Lanka, and Brazil, forming the basis of a worldwide trading network. Amsterdam's merchants had the largest share in both the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a>. These companies acquired overseas possessions that later became <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch colonies</a>.
</p><p>Amsterdam was Europe's most important point for the shipment of goods and was the leading <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">Financial centre</a> of the western world.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In 1602, the Amsterdam office of the international trading Dutch East India Company became the world's first <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> by trading in its own shares.<sup id="cite_ref-The_oldest_share_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_oldest_share-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The Bank of Amsterdam started operations in 1609, acting as a full service bank for Dutch merchant bankers and as a reserve bank.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline_and_modernisation">Decline and modernisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Decline and modernisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Amsterdam's prosperity declined during the 18th and early 19th centuries. The <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Dutch_Wars" title="Anglo-Dutch Wars">wars</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a> with <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a> and France took their toll on Amsterdam. During the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, Amsterdam's significance reached its lowest point, with Holland being absorbed into the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">French Empire</a>. However, the later establishment of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="United Kingdom of the Netherlands">United Kingdom of the Netherlands</a> in 1815 marked a turning point.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old-Amsterdam_1891-street-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Old-Amsterdam_1891-street-1.jpg/170px-Old-Amsterdam_1891-street-1.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Old-Amsterdam_1891-street-1.jpg/255px-Old-Amsterdam_1891-street-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Old-Amsterdam_1891-street-1.jpg/340px-Old-Amsterdam_1891-street-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="618" data-file-height="660" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old-Amsterdam_1891-street-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of Vijzelstraat looking towards the <a href="/wiki/Muntplein,_Amsterdam" title="Muntplein, Amsterdam">Muntplein</a>, 1891.</div></div></div>
<p>The end of the 19th century is sometimes called Amsterdam's second Golden Age.<sup id="cite_ref-Amsterdam_City_Walks_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amsterdam_City_Walks-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> New museums, a railway station, and the <a href="/wiki/Concertgebouw" title="Concertgebouw">Concertgebouw</a> were built; in this same time, the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> reached the city. The <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam%E2%80%93Rhine_Canal" title="Amsterdam–Rhine Canal">Amsterdam–Rhine Canal</a> was dug to give Amsterdam a direct connection to the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_Canal" title="North Sea Canal">North Sea Canal</a> was dug to give the port a shorter connection to the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>. Both projects dramatically improved commerce with the rest of Europe and the world. In 1906, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Conrad" title="Joseph Conrad">Joseph Conrad</a> gave a brief description of Amsterdam as seen from the seaside, in <i>The Mirror of the Sea</i>.
</p>
<h3><span id="20th_century.E2.80.93present"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century–present">20th century–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 20th century–present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_photochrom2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Amsterdam_photochrom2.jpg/220px-Amsterdam_photochrom2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Amsterdam_photochrom2.jpg/330px-Amsterdam_photochrom2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Amsterdam_photochrom2.jpg/440px-Amsterdam_photochrom2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3288" data-file-height="2396" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_photochrom2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Photochrom of Amsterdam's Dam Square at the beginning of the 20th century.</div></div></div>
<p>Shortly before the First World War, the city started to expand again, and new suburbs were built. Even though the Netherlands remained neutral in this war, Amsterdam suffered a food shortage, and heating fuel became scarce. The shortages sparked riots in which several people were killed. These riots are known as the <i>Aardappeloproer</i> (Potato rebellion). People started looting stores and warehouses in order to get supplies, mainly food.<sup id="cite_ref-aardappeloproer_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aardappeloproer-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 January 1921, after a flood in 1916, the depleted municipalities of Durgerdam, Holysloot, Zunderdorp and <a href="/wiki/Schellingwoude" title="Schellingwoude">Schellingwoude</a>, all lying north of Amsterdam, were, at their own request, annexed to the city.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Between the wars, the city continued to expand, most notably to the west of the <a href="/wiki/Jordaan" title="Jordaan">Jordaan</a> district in the <a href="/wiki/Frederik_Hendrikbuurt" title="Frederik Hendrikbuurt">Frederik Hendrikbuurt</a> and surrounding neighbourhoods.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Netherlands" title="Battle of the Netherlands">invaded the Netherlands</a> on 10 May 1940 and took control of the country. Some Amsterdam citizens sheltered Jews, thereby exposing themselves and their families to a high risk of being imprisoned or sent to concentration camps. More than 100,000 <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch Jews">Dutch Jews</a> were deported to <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">Nazi concentration camps</a>, of whom some 60,000 lived in Amsterdam. In response, the Dutch Communist Party organised the <a href="/wiki/February_strike" title="February strike">February strike</a> attended by 300,000 people to protest against the raids. Perhaps the most famous deportee was the young Jewish girl <a href="/wiki/Anne_Frank" title="Anne Frank">Anne Frank</a>, who died in the <a href="/wiki/Bergen-Belsen_concentration_camp" title="Bergen-Belsen concentration camp">Bergen-Belsen concentration camp</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-deportation_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deportation-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> At the end of the Second World War, communication with the rest of the country broke down, and food and fuel became scarce. Many citizens travelled to the countryside to forage. Dogs, cats, <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">raw sugar</a> beets, and <a href="/wiki/Tulip" title="Tulip">Tulip</a> bulbs—cooked to a pulp—were consumed to stay alive.<sup id="cite_ref-hongerwinter_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hongerwinter-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Most of the trees in Amsterdam were cut down for fuel, and all the wood was taken from the apartments of deported Jews.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Enorme_menigte_op_de_Amstellaan_te_Amsterdam_Op_de_achtergrond_de_zgn_wolkenkrabber,_Bestanddeelnr_900-2830.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Enorme_menigte_op_de_Amstellaan_te_Amsterdam_Op_de_achtergrond_de_zgn_wolkenkrabber%2C_Bestanddeelnr_900-2830.jpg/170px-Enorme_menigte_op_de_Amstellaan_te_Amsterdam_Op_de_achtergrond_de_zgn_wolkenkrabber%2C_Bestanddeelnr_900-2830.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Enorme_menigte_op_de_Amstellaan_te_Amsterdam_Op_de_achtergrond_de_zgn_wolkenkrabber%2C_Bestanddeelnr_900-2830.jpg/255px-Enorme_menigte_op_de_Amstellaan_te_Amsterdam_Op_de_achtergrond_de_zgn_wolkenkrabber%2C_Bestanddeelnr_900-2830.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Enorme_menigte_op_de_Amstellaan_te_Amsterdam_Op_de_achtergrond_de_zgn_wolkenkrabber%2C_Bestanddeelnr_900-2830.jpg/340px-Enorme_menigte_op_de_Amstellaan_te_Amsterdam_Op_de_achtergrond_de_zgn_wolkenkrabber%2C_Bestanddeelnr_900-2830.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2891" data-file-height="2869" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Enorme_menigte_op_de_Amstellaan_te_Amsterdam_Op_de_achtergrond_de_zgn_wolkenkrabber,_Bestanddeelnr_900-2830.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>People celebrating the <a href="/wiki/Liberation_Day_(Netherlands)" title="Liberation Day (Netherlands)">liberation of the Netherlands</a> at the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> on 8 May 1945.</div></div></div>
<p>Many new suburbs, such as <a href="/wiki/Osdorp" title="Osdorp">Osdorp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slotervaart_(neighborhood)" class="mw-redirect" title="Slotervaart (neighborhood)">Slotervaart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slotermeer" title="Slotermeer">Slotermeer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geuzenveld" title="Geuzenveld">Geuzenveld</a>, were built in the years after the Second World War.<sup id="cite_ref-svgeschedenis_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-svgeschedenis-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
These suburbs contained many public parks and wide open spaces, and the new buildings provided improved housing conditions with larger and brighter rooms, gardens, and balconies. Because of the war and other events of the 20th century, almost the entire city centre had fallen into disrepair. As society was changing,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> politicians and other influential figures made plans to redesign large parts of it. There was an increasing demand for office buildings, and also for new roads, as the automobile became available to most people.<sup id="cite_ref-stadsherstel_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stadsherstel-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Metro" title="Amsterdam Metro">metro</a> started operating in 1977 between the new suburb of <a href="/wiki/Bijlmermeer" title="Bijlmermeer">Bijlmermeer</a> in the city's <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam-Zuidoost" title="Amsterdam-Zuidoost">Zuidoost</a> (southeast) exclave and the centre of Amsterdam. Further plans were to build a new highway above the metro to connect <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Centraal_station" title="Amsterdam Centraal station">Amsterdam Centraal</a> and city centre with other parts of the city.
</p><p>The required large-scale demolitions began in Amsterdam's former Jewish neighbourhood. Smaller streets, such as the Jodenbreestraat, were widened and almost all of their houses were demolished. At the peak of the demolition, the <i>Nieuwmarktrellen</i> (<a href="/wiki/Nieuwmarkt_Riots" title="Nieuwmarkt Riots">Nieuwmarkt Riots</a>) broke out;<sup id="cite_ref-metrostad_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metrostad-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> the rioters expressed their fury about the demolition caused by the restructuring of the city.
</p><p>As a result, the demolition was stopped and the highway was never built; only the metro was completed. Only a few streets remained widened. The new city hall was built on the almost completely demolished Waterlooplein. Meanwhile, large private organisations, such as <i>Stadsherstel Amsterdam</i>, were founded with the aim of restoring the entire city centre. Although the success of this struggle is visible today, efforts for further restoration are still ongoing.<sup id="cite_ref-stadsherstel_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stadsherstel-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The entire city centre has reattained its former splendour and, as a whole, is now a <a href="/wiki/Protected_area" title="Protected area">protected area</a>. Many of its buildings have become monuments, and in July 2010 the <a href="/wiki/Grachtengordel_(Amsterdam)" class="mw-redirect" title="Grachtengordel (Amsterdam)">Grachtengordel</a> (the three concentric canals: Herengracht, Keizersgracht, and Prinsengracht) was added to the <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage List</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-unesco_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unesco-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Canal_Tour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Amsterdam_Canal_Tour.jpg/220px-Amsterdam_Canal_Tour.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Amsterdam_Canal_Tour.jpg/330px-Amsterdam_Canal_Tour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Amsterdam_Canal_Tour.jpg/440px-Amsterdam_Canal_Tour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="2400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Canal_Tour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 17th-century <a href="/wiki/Canals_of_Amsterdam" title="Canals of Amsterdam">Canals of Amsterdam</a> were listed as <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage site">World Heritage site</a> in 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> contributing to Amsterdam's fame as the "<a href="/wiki/Venice_of_the_North" title="Venice of the North">Venice of the North</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Venice1_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Venice1-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Venice3_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Venice3-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Along with <a href="/wiki/De_Wallen" title="De Wallen">De Wallen</a>, the canals are the focal-point for tourists in the city.</div></div></div>
<p>In the early years of the 21st century, the Amsterdam city centre has attracted large numbers of tourists: between 2012 and 2015, the annual number of visitors rose from 10 million to 17 million. Real estate prices have surged, and local shops are making way for tourist-oriented ones, making the centre unaffordable for the city's inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> These developments have evoked comparisons with <a href="/wiki/Venice_(Italy)" class="mw-redirect" title="Venice (Italy)">Venice</a>, a city thought to be overwhelmed by the tourist influx.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Construction of a metro line connecting the part of the city north of the river (or lake) <a href="/wiki/IJ_(Amsterdam)" title="IJ (Amsterdam)">IJ</a> to the centre was started in 2003. The project was controversial because its cost had exceeded its budget by a factor three by 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> because of fears of damage to buildings in the centre, and because construction had to be halted and restarted multiple times.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The metro line was completed in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2014, renewed focus has been given to urban regeneration and renewal, especially in areas directly bordering the city centre, such as <a href="/wiki/Frederik_Hendrikbuurt" title="Frederik Hendrikbuurt">Frederik Hendrikbuurt</a>. This urban renewal and expansion of the traditional centre of the city—with the construction on artificial islands of the new eastern <a href="/wiki/IJburg" title="IJburg">IJburg</a> neighbourhood—is part of the Structural Vision Amsterdam 2040 initiative.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:417px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_with_North_Sea_Canal_by_Sentinel-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Amsterdam_with_North_Sea_Canal_by_Sentinel-2.jpg/415px-Amsterdam_with_North_Sea_Canal_by_Sentinel-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="415" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Amsterdam_with_North_Sea_Canal_by_Sentinel-2.jpg/623px-Amsterdam_with_North_Sea_Canal_by_Sentinel-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Amsterdam_with_North_Sea_Canal_by_Sentinel-2.jpg/830px-Amsterdam_with_North_Sea_Canal_by_Sentinel-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4669" data-file-height="2901" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_with_North_Sea_Canal_by_Sentinel-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satellite picture of Amsterdam and North Sea Canal</div></div></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:418px;max-width:418px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:212px;max-width:212px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam-plaats-OpenTopo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Amsterdam-plaats-OpenTopo.jpg/210px-Amsterdam-plaats-OpenTopo.jpg" decoding="async" width="210" height="177" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Amsterdam-plaats-OpenTopo.jpg/315px-Amsterdam-plaats-OpenTopo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Amsterdam-plaats-OpenTopo.jpg/420px-Amsterdam-plaats-OpenTopo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5937" data-file-height="5002" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Topographic map of Amsterdam and its surrounding municipalities, 2014.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam-centrum-OpenTopo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Amsterdam-centrum-OpenTopo.jpg/200px-Amsterdam-centrum-OpenTopo.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="176" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Amsterdam-centrum-OpenTopo.jpg/300px-Amsterdam-centrum-OpenTopo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Amsterdam-centrum-OpenTopo.jpg/400px-Amsterdam-centrum-OpenTopo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10050" data-file-height="8825" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Large-scale map of the city centre of Amsterdam, including sightseeing markers, as of April&#160;2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam is located in the Western Netherlands, in the province of <a href="/wiki/North_Holland" title="North Holland">North Holland</a>, although it is not its capital which is <a href="/wiki/Haarlem" title="Haarlem">Haarlem</a>. The river <a href="/wiki/Amstel" title="Amstel">Amstel</a> ends in the city centre and connects to a large number of canals that eventually terminate in the <a href="/wiki/IJ_(Amsterdam)" title="IJ (Amsterdam)">IJ</a>. Amsterdam is about 2 metres (6.6 feet) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">below sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-elevation_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elevation-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The surrounding land is flat as it is formed of large <a href="/wiki/Polder" title="Polder">polders</a>. A man-made forest, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdamse_Bos" title="Amsterdamse Bos">Amsterdamse Bos</a>, is in the southwest. Amsterdam is connected to the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> through the long <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_Canal" title="North Sea Canal">North Sea Canal</a>.
</p><p>Amsterdam is intensely urbanised, as is the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_metropolitan_area" title="Amsterdam metropolitan area">Amsterdam metropolitan area</a> surrounding the city. Comprising 219.4 square kilometres (84.7 square miles) of land, the <a href="/wiki/City_limits" title="City limits">city proper</a> has 4,457 inhabitants per km<sup>2</sup> and 2,275 houses per km<sup>2</sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-density_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-density-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Parks and <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">nature reserves</a> make up 12% of Amsterdam's land area.<sup id="cite_ref-12percent_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12percent-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1210_Amsterdamse_grachten_101a.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/1210_Amsterdamse_grachten_101a.JPG/220px-1210_Amsterdamse_grachten_101a.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/1210_Amsterdamse_grachten_101a.JPG/330px-1210_Amsterdamse_grachten_101a.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/1210_Amsterdamse_grachten_101a.JPG/440px-1210_Amsterdamse_grachten_101a.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="1790" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1210_Amsterdamse_grachten_101a.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Reguliersgracht, Autumn 2010.</div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam has more than 100 kilometres (60 miles) of <a href="/wiki/Canals_of_Amsterdam" title="Canals of Amsterdam">canals</a>, most of which are navigable by boat. The city's three main canals are the Prinsengracht, Herengracht, and Keizersgracht.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, Amsterdam was surrounded by a moat, called the <a href="/wiki/Singel" title="Singel">Singel</a>, which now forms the innermost ring in the city, and makes the city centre a horseshoe shape. The city is also served by a <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Amsterdam" title="Port of Amsterdam">seaport</a>. It has been compared with <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>, due to its division into about 90 islands, which are linked by more than 1,200 bridges.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nieuwendammerdijk,_Amsterdam,_North_Holland,_Netherlands_-_panoramio_(3).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Nieuwendammerdijk%2C_Amsterdam%2C_North_Holland%2C_Netherlands_-_panoramio_%283%29.jpg/220px-Nieuwendammerdijk%2C_Amsterdam%2C_North_Holland%2C_Netherlands_-_panoramio_%283%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Nieuwendammerdijk%2C_Amsterdam%2C_North_Holland%2C_Netherlands_-_panoramio_%283%29.jpg/330px-Nieuwendammerdijk%2C_Amsterdam%2C_North_Holland%2C_Netherlands_-_panoramio_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Nieuwendammerdijk%2C_Amsterdam%2C_North_Holland%2C_Netherlands_-_panoramio_%283%29.jpg/440px-Nieuwendammerdijk%2C_Amsterdam%2C_North_Holland%2C_Netherlands_-_panoramio_%283%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nieuwendammerdijk,_Amsterdam,_North_Holland,_Netherlands_-_panoramio_(3).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winter 2010 in <a href="/wiki/Nieuwendammerdijk_en_Buiksloterdijk" title="Nieuwendammerdijk en Buiksloterdijk">Nieuwendammerdijk en Buiksloterdijk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam-Noord" title="Amsterdam-Noord">Amsterdam-Noord</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam has an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a> <i>Cfb</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> strongly influenced by its proximity to the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> to the west, with prevailing westerly winds. While winters and summers are generally mild, temperatures can vary year by year.  There can occasionally be cold snowy winters and hot humid summers.
</p><p>Amsterdam, as well as most of the North Holland province, lies in <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Agriculture" title="United States Department of Agriculture">USDA</a> <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">Hardiness zone</a> 8b. Frosts mainly occur during spells of easterly or northeasterly winds from the inner European continent. Even then, because Amsterdam is surrounded on three sides by large bodies of water, as well as having a significant <a href="/wiki/Urban_heat_island" title="Urban heat island">heat-island effect</a>, nights rarely fall below −5&#160;°C (23&#160;°F), while it could easily be −12&#160;°C (10&#160;°F) in Hilversum, 25 kilometres (16 miles) southeast.
</p><p>Summers are moderately warm with a number of hot days every month. The average daily high in August is 22.1&#160;°C (71.8&#160;°F), and 30&#160;°C (86&#160;°F) or higher is only measured on average on 2.5 days, placing Amsterdam in AHS Heat Zone 2. The record extremes range from −19.7&#160;°C (−3.5&#160;°F) to 36.3&#160;°C (97.3&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Extreme_temps_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Extreme_temps-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Extreme_temps_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Extreme_temps-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
Days with more than 1 millimetre (0.04&#160;in) of <a href="/wiki/Precipitation" title="Precipitation">precipitation</a> are common, on average 133 days per year.
</p><p>Amsterdam's average annual precipitation is 838 millimetres (33&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> A large part of this precipitation falls as light rain or brief showers. Cloudy and damp days are common during the cooler months of October through March.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_population">Historical population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Historical population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="toccolours" style="width:30em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><tbody><tr><th class="navbox-title" colspan="2" style="padding:0.25em;font-size:110%">Estimated population, 1300–1564</th></tr><tr valign="top"><td style="padding:0 0.5em"><table style="border-spacing:0;width:15em"><tbody><tr style="font-size:95%"><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;width:3em">Year</th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px 2px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Population">Pop.</abbr></th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Per annum growth rate">±% p.a.</abbr></th></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1300</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">1,000</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">—&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1400</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">4,700</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+1.56%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1514</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">11,000</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+0.75%</td></tr></tbody></table></td><td style="padding:0 0.5em;border-left:solid 1px #aaa"><table style="border-spacing:0;width:15em"><tbody><tr style="font-size:95%"><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;width:3em">Year</th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px 2px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Population">Pop.</abbr></th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Per annum growth rate">±% p.a.</abbr></th></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1546</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">13,200</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+0.57%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">1557</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">22,200</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">+4.84%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1564</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">30,900</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+4.84%</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">Source: Bureau Monumentenzorg en Archeologie (1300)<sup id="cite_ref-BMA_Gesch1_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BMA_Gesch1-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><br /><a href="#CITEREFRamaer1921">Ramaer 1921</a>, pp.&#160;11–12, 181 (1400 and 1564)<br /><a href="#CITEREFVan_Dillen1929">Van Dillen 1929</a>, pp.&#160;xxv–xxvi (1514, 1546 and 1557)</td></tr></tbody></table><p>In 1300, Amsterdam's population was around 1,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> While many towns in Holland experienced population decline during the 15th and 16th centuries, Amsterdam's population grew,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> mainly due to the rise of the profitable <a href="/wiki/Baltic_maritime_trade_(c._1400%E2%80%931800)" title="Baltic maritime trade (c. 1400–1800)">Baltic maritime trade</a> after the Burgundian victory in the <a href="/wiki/Dutch%E2%80%93Hanseatic_War" title="Dutch–Hanseatic War">Dutch–Hanseatic War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Still, the population of Amsterdam was only modest compared to the towns and cities of <a href="/wiki/County_of_Flanders" title="County of Flanders">Flanders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brabant" title="Duchy of Brabant">Brabant</a>, which comprised the most urbanised area of the Low Countries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></p><table class="toccolours" style="width:30em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><tbody><tr><th style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">−4.2%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1790</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">214,473</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">−6.3%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1800</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">203,485</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">−5.1%</td></tr></tbody></table></td><td style="padding:0 0.5em;border-left:solid 1px #aaa"><table style="border-spacing:0;width:15em"><tbody><tr style="text-align:right;padding:1px">520,602</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+24.7%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1910</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">647,427</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+12.8%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">1930</th><td style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1940</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">800,594</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+5.7%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1950</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">835,834</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+4.4%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1960</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">869,602</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+4.0%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1970</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">831,463</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">−4.4%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">1980</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">716,967</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">−13.8%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1990</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">695,221</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">−3.0%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2000</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">731,289</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+5.2%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2010</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">767,773</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+5.0%</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">Source: <a href="#CITEREFNusteling1985">Nusteling 1985</a>, p.&#160;240 (1590–1670)<br /><a href="#CITEREFVan_LeeuwenOeppen1993">Van Leeuwen &amp; Oeppen 1993</a>, p.&#160;87 (1680–1880)<br /><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://os.cijfersinbeeld.net/amsterdamincijfers/#bevolking">Department for Research, Information and Statistics</a> (1890–present)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>This changed when, during the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Revolt" title="Dutch Revolt">Dutch Revolt</a>, many people from the Southern Netherlands fled to the North, especially after <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Antwerp" title="Fall of Antwerp">Antwerp fell to Spanish forces</a> in 1585. Jewish people from Spain, Portugal and Eastern Europe similarly settled in Amsterdam, as did Germans and Scandinavians.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In thirty years, Amsterdam's population more than doubled from 1585 to 1610.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> By 1600, its population was around 50,000.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> During the 1660s, Amsterdam's population reached 200,000.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The city's growth levelled off and the population stabilised around 240,000 for most of the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1750, Amsterdam was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_European_cities_in_history" title="List of largest European cities in history">fourth largest city in western Europe</a>, behind London (676,000), Paris (560,000) and Naples (324,000).<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> This was all the more remarkable as Amsterdam was neither the capital city nor the seat of government of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>, which itself was a much smaller state than England, France or the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. In contrast to those other metropolises, Amsterdam was also surrounded by large towns such as <a href="/wiki/Leiden" title="Leiden">Leiden</a> (about 67,000), <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> (45,000), <a href="/wiki/Haarlem" title="Haarlem">Haarlem</a> (38,000), and <a href="/wiki/Utrecht" title="Utrecht">Utrecht</a> (30,000).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrijhoffPrak20059_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrijhoffPrak20059-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city's population declined in the early 19th century,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> dipping under 200,000 in 1820.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> By the second half of the 19th century, industrialisation spurred renewed growth.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Amsterdam's population hit an all-time high of 872,000 in 1959,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> before declining in the following decades due to government-sponsored suburbanisation to so-called <i>groeikernen</i> (growth centres) such as <a href="/wiki/Purmerend" title="Purmerend">Purmerend</a> and <a href="/wiki/Almere" title="Almere">Almere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Between 1970 and 1980, Amsterdam experienced its sharp population decline, peaking at a net loss of 25,000 people in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> By 1985 the city had only 675,570 residents.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> This was soon followed by <a href="/wiki/Reurbanization" class="mw-redirect" title="Reurbanization">reurbanisation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">gentrification</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_83-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> leading to renewed population growth in the 2010s. Also in the 2010s, much of Amsterdam's population growth was due to immigration to the city.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Amsterdam's population is expected to top its previous high in 2019, reaching 873,000.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Immigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>In the 16th and 17th century non-Dutch immigrants to Amsterdam were mostly <a href="/wiki/Huguenot" class="mw-redirect" title="Huguenot">Huguenots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flemish_people" title="Flemish people">Flemings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardi Jews</a> and <a href="/wiki/Westphalia" title="Westphalia">Westphalians</a>. Huguenots came after the <a href="/wiki/Edict_of_Fontainebleau" title="Edict of Fontainebleau">Edict of Fontainebleau</a> in 1685, while the Flemish Protestants came during the <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years&#39; War">Eighty Years' War</a>. The Westphalians came to Amsterdam mostly for economic reasons – their influx continued through the 18th and 19th centuries. Before the Second World War, 10% of the city population was <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Amsterdam" title="History of the Jews in Amsterdam">Jewish</a>. Just twenty per cent of them survived the <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">Shoah</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first mass immigration in the 20th century were by people from Indonesia, who came to Amsterdam after the independence of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> in the 1940s and 1950s. In the 1960s <a href="/wiki/Foreign_worker" title="Foreign worker">guest workers</a> from Turkey, Morocco, Italy and Spain emigrated to Amsterdam. After the independence of Suriname in 1975, a large wave of Surinamese settled in Amsterdam, mostly in the <a href="/wiki/Bijlmermeer" title="Bijlmermeer">Bijlmer</a> area. Other immigrants, including refugees <a href="/wiki/Right_of_asylum" title="Right of asylum">asylum seekers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration" title="Illegal immigration">illegal immigrants</a>, came from Europe, <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">America</a>, Asia, and Africa. In the 1970s and 1980s, many 'old' Amsterdammers moved to 'new' cities like <a href="/wiki/Almere" title="Almere">Almere</a> and <a href="/wiki/Purmerend" title="Purmerend">Purmerend</a>, prompted by the third <a href="/wiki/Land-use_planning" title="Land-use planning">planological</a> bill of the Dutch government. This bill promoted suburbanisation and arranged for new developments in so-called "groeikernen", literally <i>cores of growth</i>. Young professionals and artists moved into neighbourhoods de Pijp and the <a href="/wiki/Jordaan" title="Jordaan">Jordaan</a> abandoned by these Amsterdammers. The non-Western immigrants settled mostly in the <a href="/wiki/Public_housing" title="Public housing">social housing</a> projects in Amsterdam-West and the Bijlmer. Today, people of non-Western origin make up approximately one-third of the population of Amsterdam, and more than 50% of the city'
s children.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OS_4351_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OS_4351-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Ethnic Dutch (as <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people#Ethnic_identity" title="Dutch people">defined</a> by the Dutch census) now make up a minority of the total population, although by far the largest one. Only one in three inhabitants under 15 is an <i>autochtoon</i>, or a person who has two parents of Dutch origin.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Segregation along ethnic lines is clearly visible, with people of non-Western origin, considered a separate group by <a href="/wiki/Statistics_Netherlands" title="Statistics Netherlands">Statistics Netherlands</a>, concentrating in specific neighbourhoods especially in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Nieuw-West" title="Amsterdam Nieuw-West">Nieuw-West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zeeburg" title="Zeeburg">Zeeburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bijlmermeer" title="Bijlmermeer">Bijlmer</a> and in certain areas of <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam-Noord" title="Amsterdam-Noord">Amsterdam-Noord</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2000, Christians formed the largest <a href="/wiki/Religious_denomination" title="Religious denomination">religious group</a> in the city (17% of the population). The next largest religion was Islam (14%), most of whose followers were <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-religion_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
