<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Religions in Amsterdam (2015)<sup id="cite_ref-random_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-random-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:WhiteSmoke; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">Non affiliated</a> (62.2%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_Netherlands" title="Islam in the Netherlands">Islam</a> (12.1%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkOrchid; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> (11.2%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Protestant_Church_in_the_Netherlands" title="Protestant Church in the Netherlands">Protestant Church in the Netherlands</a> (5.9%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DeepSkyBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other Christian denominations (5.9%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Orange; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> (1.1%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Yellow; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (1.0%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Blue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> (0.7%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<p>In 1578, the largely Roman Catholic city of Amsterdam joined the revolt against Spanish rule,<sup id="cite_ref-:3_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> late in comparison to other major northern Dutch cities.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Roman Catholic priests were driven out of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Following the Dutch takeover, all churches were converted to Protestant worship.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a> was declared the main religion,<sup id="cite_ref-:4_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> and although Catholicism was not forbidden and priests allowed to serve, the <a href="/wiki/Hierarchy_of_the_Catholic_Church" title="Hierarchy of the Catholic Church">Catholic hierarchy</a> was prohibited.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (February 2019)">dubious</span></a>&#32;<span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Amsterdam#Dubious" title="Talk:Amsterdam">discuss</a></span></i>&#93;</sup> This led to the establishment of <i>schuilkerken</i>, covert religious buildings that were hidden in pre-existing buildings. Catholics, some Jewish and dissenting Protestants worshiped in such buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> A large influx of foreigners of many religions came to 17th-century Amsterdam, in particular <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sefardic Jews</a> from Spain and Portugal,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Huguenot" class="mw-redirect" title="Huguenot">Huguenots</a> from France,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutherans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mennonites" title="Mennonites">Mennonites</a>, and Protestants from across the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> This led to the establishment of many non-Dutch-speaking churches.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In 1603, the Jewish received permission to practice their religion. In 1639, the first synagogue was consecrated.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The Jews came to call the town <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem_of_the_West" title="Jerusalem of the West">Jerusalem of the West</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As they became established in the city, other <a href="/wiki/Christian_denomination" title="Christian denomination">Christian denominations</a> used converted Catholic chapels to conduct their own services. The oldest English-language church congregation in the world outside the United Kingdom is found at the <a href="/wiki/Begijnhof,_Amsterdam" title="Begijnhof, Amsterdam">Begijnhof</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Regular services there are still offered in English under the auspices of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-englishchurch_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-englishchurch-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Being Calvinists, the Huguenots soon integrated into the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Reformed_Church" title="Dutch Reformed Church">Dutch Reformed Church</a>, though often retaining their own congregations. Some, commonly referred by the moniker 'Walloon', are recognisable today as they offer occasional services in French.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In the second half of the 17th century, Amsterdam experienced an influx of <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Ashkenazim</a>, Jews from <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central and Eastern Europe</a>. Jews often fled the <a href="/wiki/Pogrom" title="Pogrom">pogroms</a> in those areas. The first Ashkenazi who arrived in Amsterdam were <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Khmelnytsky_Uprising" title="Khmelnytsky Uprising">Khmelnytsky Uprising</a> in eastern Poland and the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years&#39; War">Thirty Years' War</a>. They not only founded their own synagogues, but had a strong influence on the 'Amsterdam dialect' adding a large <a href="/wiki/Yiddish_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Yiddish language">Yiddish</a> local vocabulary.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite an absence of an official Jewish <a href="/wiki/Ghetto" title="Ghetto">ghetto</a>, most Jews preferred to live in the eastern part of the old medieval heart of the city. The main street of this Jewish neighbourhood was the <i>Jodenbreestraat</i>. The neighbourhood comprised the <i>Waterlooplein</i> and the <a href="/wiki/Nieuwmarkt" title="Nieuwmarkt">Nieuwmarkt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jodenbuurt_Amsterdam_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jodenbuurt_Amsterdam-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Buildings in this neighbourhood fell into disrepair after the Second World War,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> and a large section of the neighbourhood was demolished during the construction of the subway. This led to riots, and as a result the original plans for large-scale reconstruction were abandoned.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The neighbourhood was rebuilt with smaller-scale residence buildings on the basis of its original layout.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Westerkerk_Amsterdam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Westerkerk_Amsterdam.jpg/220px-Westerkerk_Amsterdam.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Westerkerk_Amsterdam.jpg/330px-Westerkerk_Amsterdam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Westerkerk_Amsterdam.jpg/440px-Westerkerk_Amsterdam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3995" data-file-height="3478" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Westerkerk_Amsterdam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Westerkerk" title="Westerkerk">Westerkerk</a> in the Centrum borough, one of Amsterdam's best known churches.</div></div></div>
<p>Catholic churches in Amsterdam have been constructed since the restoration of the episcopal hierarchy in 1853.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> One of the principal architects behind the city's Catholic churches, <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Cuypers" title="Pierre Cuypers">Cuypers</a>, was also responsible for the Amsterdam Central station and the <a href="/wiki/Rijksmuseum" title="Rijksmuseum">Rijksmuseum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1924, the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> of the Netherlands hosted the <a href="/wiki/Eucharistic_Congress" class="mw-redirect" title="Eucharistic Congress">International Eucharistic Congress</a> in Amsterdam,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> and numerous Catholic <a href="/wiki/Prelate" title="Prelate">prelates</a> visited the city, where festivities were held in churches and stadiums.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Catholic processions on the public streets, however, were still forbidden under law at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Only in the 20th century was Amsterdam's relation to Catholicism normalised,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> but despite its far larger <a href="/wiki/Population_size" title="Population size">population size</a>, the episcopal see of the city was placed in the provincial town of <a href="/wiki/Haarlem" title="Haarlem">Haarlem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Diocese_of_Haarlem_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diocese_of_Haarlem-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In recent times, religious demographics in Amsterdam have been changed by immigration from former colonies. <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> has been introduced from the Hindu diaspora from Suriname<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> and several distinct branches of Islam have been brought from various parts of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Islam is now the largest non-Christian religion in Amsterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-random_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-random-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The large community of Ghanaian immigrants have established African churches,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> often in parking garages in the <a href="/wiki/Bijlmermeer" title="Bijlmermeer">Bijlmer</a> area.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diversity_and_immigration">Diversity and immigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Diversity and immigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Amsterdam experienced an influx of religions and cultures after the Second World War. With 180 different nationalities,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Amsterdam is home to one of the widest varieties of nationalities of any city in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> The proportion of the population of immigrant origin in the city proper is about 50%<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> and 88% of the population are Dutch citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Amsterdam has been one of the municipalities in the Netherlands which provided immigrants with extensive and free <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch-language</a> courses, which have benefited many immigrants.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape_and_architecture">Cityscape and architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Cityscape and architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Amsterdam" title="List of tallest buildings in Amsterdam">List of tallest buildings in Amsterdam</a></div>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Cityscape.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Amsterdam_Cityscape.jpg/800px-Amsterdam_Cityscape.jpg" decoding="async" width="800" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Amsterdam_Cityscape.jpg/1200px-Amsterdam_Cityscape.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Amsterdam_Cityscape.jpg/1600px-Amsterdam_Cityscape.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="1503" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Cityscape.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center>View of the city centre looking southwest from the Oosterdokskade.</center></div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_in_1538.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Amsterdam_in_1538.JPG/330px-Amsterdam_in_1538.JPG" decoding="async" width="330" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Amsterdam_in_1538.JPG/495px-Amsterdam_in_1538.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Amsterdam_in_1538.JPG/660px-Amsterdam_in_1538.JPG 2x" data-file-width="6400" data-file-height="4138" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_in_1538.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 1538 painting by <a href="/wiki/Cornelis_Anthonisz" class="mw-redirect" title="Cornelis Anthonisz">Cornelis Anthonisz</a> showing a bird's-eye view of Amsterdam; the famous <a href="/wiki/Canals_of_Amsterdam" title="Canals of Amsterdam">Grachtengordel</a> had not yet been established.</div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam fans out south from the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Centraal_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Centraal railway station">Amsterdam Centraal railway station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Damrak" title="Damrak">Damrak</a>, the main street off the station. The oldest area of the town is known as <a href="/wiki/De_Wallen" title="De Wallen">De Wallen</a> (English: "The Quays"). It lies to the east of Damrak and contains the city's famous red light district. To the south of De Wallen is the old Jewish quarter of Waterlooplein.
</p><p>The medieval and colonial age <a href="/wiki/Canals_of_Amsterdam" title="Canals of Amsterdam">canals of Amsterdam</a>, known as <i>grachten</i>, embraces the heart of the city where homes have interesting gables. Beyond the Grachtengordel are the former working class areas of <a href="/wiki/Jordaan" title="Jordaan">Jordaan</a> and de Pijp. The <a href="/wiki/Museumplein" title="Museumplein">Museumplein</a> with the city's major museums, the <a href="/wiki/Vondelpark" title="Vondelpark">Vondelpark</a>, a 19th-century park named after the Dutch writer <a href="/wiki/Joost_van_den_Vondel" title="Joost van den Vondel">Joost van den Vondel</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Plantage_(Amsterdam)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantage (Amsterdam)">Plantage</a> neighbourhood, with the <a href="/wiki/Natura_Artis_Magistra" title="Natura Artis Magistra">zoo</a>, are also located outside the Grachtengordel.
</p><p>Several parts of the city and the surrounding urban area are <a href="/wiki/Polder" title="Polder">polders</a>. This can be recognised by the suffix <i>-meer</i> which means <i>lake</i>, as in <a href="/wiki/Aalsmeer" title="Aalsmeer">Aalsmeer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bijlmermeer" title="Bijlmermeer">Bijlmermeer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haarlemmermeer" title="Haarlemmermeer">Haarlemmermeer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Watergraafsmeer" title="Watergraafsmeer">Watergraafsmeer</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canals">Canals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Canals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Canals_of_Amsterdam" title="Canals of Amsterdam">Canals of Amsterdam</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Herengracht-december-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Herengracht-december-2.jpg/220px-Herengracht-december-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Herengracht-december-2.jpg/330px-Herengracht-december-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Herengracht-december-2.jpg/440px-Herengracht-december-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Herengracht-december-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Herengracht</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prinsengracht_towads_Lekkeresluis_from_Bridge_Prinsenstraat_2016-09-12.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Prinsengracht_towads_Lekkeresluis_from_Bridge_Prinsenstraat_2016-09-12.jpg/220px-Prinsengracht_towads_Lekkeresluis_from_Bridge_Prinsenstraat_2016-09-12.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Prinsengracht_towads_Lekkeresluis_from_Bridge_Prinsenstraat_2016-09-12.jpg/330px-Prinsengracht_towads_Lekkeresluis_from_Bridge_Prinsenstraat_2016-09-12.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Prinsengracht_towads_Lekkeresluis_from_Bridge_Prinsenstraat_2016-09-12.jpg/440px-Prinsengracht_towads_Lekkeresluis_from_Bridge_Prinsenstraat_2016-09-12.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prinsengracht_towads_Lekkeresluis_from_Bridge_Prinsenstraat_2016-09-12.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Prinsengracht</div></div></div>
<p>The Amsterdam canal system is the result of conscious <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning" title="Urban planning">city planning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-canals_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-canals-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> In the early 17th century, when immigration was at a peak, a comprehensive plan was developed that was based on four concentric half-circles of canals with their ends emerging at the <a href="/wiki/IJ_(Amsterdam)" title="IJ (Amsterdam)">IJ</a> bay. Known as the <a href="/wiki/Grachtengordel_(Amsterdam)" class="mw-redirect" title="Grachtengordel (Amsterdam)">Grachtengordel</a>, three of the canals were mostly for residential development: the Herengracht (where "Heren" refers to <i>Heren Regeerders van de stad Amsterdam</i> (ruling lords of Amsterdam), and <i><a href="/wiki/Gracht" title="Gracht">gracht</a></i> means canal, so the name can be roughly translated as "Canal of the Lords"), Keizersgracht (Emperor's Canal), and Prinsengracht (Prince's Canal).<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> The fourth and outermost canal is the <a href="/wiki/Singelgracht" title="Singelgracht">Singelgracht</a>, which is often not mentioned on maps, because it is a collective name for all canals in the outer ring. The Singelgracht should not be confused with the oldest and innermost canal, the <a href="/wiki/Singel" title="Singel">Singel</a>.
</p><p>The canals served for defence, <a href="/wiki/Water_resource_management" title="Water resource management">water management</a> and transport. The defences took the form of a moat and <a href="/wiki/Earthworks_(engineering)" title="Earthworks (engineering)">earthen dikes</a>, with gates at transit points, but otherwise no masonry <a href="/wiki/Superstructure" title="Superstructure">superstructures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> The original plans have been lost, so historians, such as Ed Taverne, need to speculate on the original intentions: it is thought that the considerations of the layout were purely practical and defensive rather than ornamental.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Construction started in 1613 and proceeded from west to east, across the breadth of the layout, like a gigantic <a href="/wiki/Windscreen_wiper" title="Windscreen wiper">windshield wiper</a> as the historian <a href="/wiki/Geert_Mak" title="Geert Mak">Geert Mak</a> calls it – and not from the centre outwards, as a popular myth has it. The canal construction in the southern sector was completed by 1656. Subsequently, the construction of residential buildings proceeded slowly. The eastern part of the concentric canal plan, covering the area between the Amstel river and the IJ bay, has never been implemented. In the following centuries, the land was used for parks, senior citizens' homes, theatres, other public facilities, and waterways without much planning.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Over the years, several canals have been filled in, becoming streets or squares, such as the <a href="/wiki/Nieuwezijds_Voorburgwal" title="Nieuwezijds Voorburgwal">Nieuwezijds Voorburgwal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Spui_(Amsterdam)" title="Spui (Amsterdam)">Spui</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-filledincanals_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filledincanals-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion">Expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Expansion_of_Amsterdam_since_the_19th_century" title="Expansion of Amsterdam since the 19th century">Expansion of Amsterdam since the 19th century</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brug_127_in_de_Lijnbaansgracht_over_de_Egelantiersgracht_foto_4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Brug_127_in_de_Lijnbaansgracht_over_de_Egelantiersgracht_foto_4.jpg/220px-Brug_127_in_de_Lijnbaansgracht_over_de_Egelantiersgracht_foto_4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Brug_127_in_de_Lijnbaansgracht_over_de_Egelantiersgracht_foto_4.jpg/330px-Brug_127_in_de_Lijnbaansgracht_over_de_Egelantiersgracht_foto_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Brug_127_in_de_Lijnbaansgracht_over_de_Egelantiersgracht_foto_4.jpg/440px-Brug_127_in_de_Lijnbaansgracht_over_de_Egelantiersgracht_foto_4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brug_127_in_de_Lijnbaansgracht_over_de_Egelantiersgracht_foto_4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Egelantiersgracht" title="Egelantiersgracht">Egelantiersgracht</a> lies west of the <a href="/wiki/Grachtengordel" title="Grachtengordel">Grachtengordel</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Jordaan" title="Jordaan">Jordaan</a> neighbourhood.</div></div></div>
<p>After the development of Amsterdam's canals in the 17th century, the city did not grow beyond its borders for two centuries. During the 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Sarphati" title="Samuel Sarphati">Samuel Sarphati</a> devised a plan based on the grandeur of Paris and London at that time. The plan envisaged the construction of new houses, public buildings and streets just outside the <a href="/wiki/Grachtengordel_(Amsterdam)" class="mw-redirect" title="Grachtengordel (Amsterdam)">Grachtengordel</a>. The main aim of the plan, however, was to improve public health. Although the plan did not expand the city, it did produce some of the largest public buildings to date, like the <i>Paleis voor Volksvlijt</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-joodsmuseum_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-joodsmuseum-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-zgsarphati_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zgsarphati-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jlgsarphati_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jlgsarphati-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following Sarphati, civil engineers Jacobus van Niftrik and Jan Kalff designed an entire ring of 19th-century neighbourhoods surrounding the city's centre, with the city preserving the ownership of all land outside the 17th-century limit, thus firmly controlling development.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Most of these neighbourhoods became home to the working class.<sup id="cite_ref-oudzuid_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oudzuid-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In response to overcrowding, two plans were designed at the beginning of the 20th century which were very different from anything Amsterdam had ever seen before: <i>Plan Zuid</i>, designed by the architect <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Petrus_Berlage" title="Hendrik Petrus Berlage">Berlage</a>, and <i>West</i>. These plans involved the development of new neighbourhoods consisting of housing blocks for all social classes.<sup id="cite_ref-archiefberlage_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archiefberlage-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bmzberlage_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmzberlage-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the Second World War, large new neighbourhoods were built in the western, southeastern, and northern parts of the city. These new neighbourhoods were built to relieve the city's shortage of living space and give people affordable houses with modern conveniences. The neighbourhoods consisted mainly of large housing blocks situated among green spaces, connected to wide roads, making the neighbourhoods easily accessible by <a href="/wiki/Car" title="Car">motor car</a>. The western suburbs which were built in that period are collectively called the Westelijke Tuinsteden. The area to the southeast of the city built during the same period is known as the Bijlmer.<sup id="cite_ref-bijlmer_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bijlmer-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-westelijketuinsteden_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-westelijketuinsteden-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Scheepvaarthuis_002.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Amsterdam_Scheepvaarthuis_002.JPG/220px-Amsterdam_Scheepvaarthuis_002.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Amsterdam_Scheepvaarthuis_002.JPG/330px-Amsterdam_Scheepvaarthuis_002.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Amsterdam_Scheepvaarthuis_002.JPG/440px-Amsterdam_Scheepvaarthuis_002.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3033" data-file-height="2121" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Scheepvaarthuis_002.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Scheepvaarthuis" title="Scheepvaarthuis">Scheepvaarthuis</a>, by architects <a href="/wiki/Johan_van_der_Mey" class="mw-redirect" title="Johan van der Mey">Johan van der Mey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michel_de_Klerk" title="Michel de Klerk">Michel de Klerk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piet_Kramer" title="Piet Kramer">Piet Kramer</a> is characteristic of the architecture of the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_School" title="Amsterdam School">Amsterdam School</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam has a rich <a href="/wiki/History_of_architecture" title="History of architecture">architectural history</a>. The oldest building in Amsterdam is the <a href="/wiki/Oude_Kerk,_Amsterdam" title="Oude Kerk, Amsterdam">Oude Kerk</a> (English: Old Church), at the heart of the Wallen, consecrated in 1306.<sup id="cite_ref-Oude_Kerk_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oude_Kerk-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> The oldest wooden building is <i>Het Houten Huys</i><sup id="cite_ref-houtenhuys_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-houtenhuys-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> at the <a href="/wiki/Begijnhof,_Amsterdam" title="Begijnhof, Amsterdam">Begijnhof</a>. It was constructed around 1425 and is one of only two existing wooden buildings. It is also one of the few examples of <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic architecture</a> in Amsterdam. The oldest stone building of the Netherlands, The Moriaan is build in <a href="/wiki/%27s-Hertogenbosch" title="&#39;s-Hertogenbosch">'s-Hertogenbosch</a>.
</p><p>In the 16th century, wooden buildings were razed and replaced with brick ones. During this period, many buildings were constructed in the <a href="/wiki/Architectural_style" title="Architectural style">architectural style</a> of the <a href="/wiki/The_Renaissance" class="mw-redirect" title="The Renaissance">Renaissance</a>. Buildings of this period are very recognisable with their <a href="/wiki/Crow-stepped_gable" title="Crow-stepped gable">stepped gable</a> façades, which is the common Dutch Renaissance style. Amsterdam quickly developed its own <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_architecture" title="Renaissance architecture">Renaissance architecture</a>. These buildings were built according to the principles of the architect <a href="/wiki/Hendrick_de_Keyser" title="Hendrick de Keyser">Hendrick de Keyser</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dekeyser_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dekeyser-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> One of the most striking buildings designed by Hendrick de Keyer is the <a href="/wiki/Westerkerk" title="Westerkerk">Westerkerk</a>. In the 17th century <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">baroque architecture</a> became very popular, as it was elsewhere in Europe. This roughly coincided with Amsterdam's <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Golden Age</a>. The leading architects of this style in Amsterdam were <a href="/wiki/Jacob_van_Campen" title="Jacob van Campen">Jacob van Campen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philips_Vingboons" title="Philips Vingboons">Philips Vingboons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dani%C3%ABl_Stalpaert" title="Daniël Stalpaert">Daniel Stalpaert</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-holclass_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holclass-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BegijnhofAmsterdamNederlandPanorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/BegijnhofAmsterdamNederlandPanorama.jpg/220px-BegijnhofAmsterdamNederlandPanorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/BegijnhofAmsterdamNederlandPanorama.jpg/330px-BegijnhofAmsterdamNederlandPanorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/BegijnhofAmsterdamNederlandPanorama.jpg/440px-BegijnhofAmsterdamNederlandPanorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6020" data-file-height="2627" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BegijnhofAmsterdamNederlandPanorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Begijnhof,_Amsterdam" title="Begijnhof, Amsterdam">Begijnhof</a> is one of the oldest <a href="/wiki/Hofje" title="Hofje">hofjes</a> in Amsterdam.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%96ffentliche_Bibliothek_und_Konservatorium_Amsterdam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/%C3%96ffentliche_Bibliothek_und_Konservatorium_Amsterdam.jpg/220px-%C3%96ffentliche_Bibliothek_und_Konservatorium_Amsterdam.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/%C3%96ffentliche_Bibliothek_und_Konservatorium_Amsterdam.jpg/330px-%C3%96ffentliche_Bibliothek_und_Konservatorium_Amsterdam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/%C3%96ffentliche_Bibliothek_und_Konservatorium_Amsterdam.jpg/440px-%C3%96ffentliche_Bibliothek_und_Konservatorium_Amsterdam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4800" data-file-height="2700" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%96ffentliche_Bibliothek_und_Konservatorium_Amsterdam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Openbare_Bibliotheek_Amsterdam" title="Openbare Bibliotheek Amsterdam">Openbare Bibliotheek Amsterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conservatorium_van_Amsterdam" title="Conservatorium van Amsterdam">Conservatorium van Amsterdam</a>, two examples of 21st-century architecture in the centre of the city.</div></div></div>
<p>Philip Vingboons designed splendid merchants' houses throughout the city. A famous building in <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">baroque style</a> in Amsterdam is the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Palace_of_Amsterdam" title="Royal Palace of Amsterdam">Royal Palace</a> on <a href="/wiki/Dam_Square" title="Dam Square">Dam Square</a>. Throughout the 18th century, Amsterdam was heavily influenced by <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_France" title="Culture of France">French culture</a>. This is reflected in the architecture of that period. Around 1815, architects broke with the baroque style and started building in different neo-styles.<sup id="cite_ref-neostijl_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neostijl-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Most Gothic style buildings date from that era and are therefore said to be built in a <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">neo-gothic</a> style. At the end of the 19th century, the <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Jugendstil</a> or <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a> style became popular and many new buildings were constructed in this architectural style. Since Amsterdam expanded rapidly during this period, new buildings adjacent to the city centre were also built in this style. The houses in the vicinity of the <a href="/wiki/Museumplein" title="Museumplein">Museum Square</a> in Amsterdam Oud-Zuid are an example of Jugendstil. The last style that was popular in Amsterdam before the <a href="/wiki/Modern_history" title="Modern history">modern era</a> was <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a>. Amsterdam had its own version of the style, which was called the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_School" title="Amsterdam School">Amsterdamse School</a>. Whole districts were built this style, such as the <i>Rivierenbuurt</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-aschool_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aschool-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> A notable feature of the façades of buildings designed in Amsterdamse School is that they are highly decorated and ornate, with oddly shaped windows and doors.
</p><p>The old city centre is the focal point of all the architectural styles before the end of the 19th century.
Jugendstil and Georgian are mostly found outside the city's centre in the neighbourhoods built in the early
20th century, although there are also some striking examples of these styles in the city centre.
Most historic buildings in the city centre and nearby are houses, such as the famous merchants' houses lining the canals.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_recreational_areas">Parks and recreational areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Parks and recreational areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_parks_in_Amsterdam" title="List of parks in Amsterdam">List of parks in Amsterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_squares_in_Amsterdam" title="List of squares in Amsterdam">List of squares in Amsterdam</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_map_indicating_parks_-_01.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Amsterdam_map_indicating_parks_-_01.png/220px-Amsterdam_map_indicating_parks_-_01.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Amsterdam_map_indicating_parks_-_01.png/330px-Amsterdam_map_indicating_parks_-_01.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Amsterdam_map_indicating_parks_-_01.png/440px-Amsterdam_map_indicating_parks_-_01.png 2x" data-file-width="1507" data-file-height="1211" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_map_indicating_parks_-_01.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="plainlist"><ul><li>A: <a exist)">Beatrixpark</a></li><li>C: <a href="/wiki/Sarphatipark" title="Sarphatipark">Sarphatipark</a></li><li>D: <a href="/wiki/Oosterpark_(Amsterdam)" title="Oosterpark href="/wiki/Westerpark_(park)" title="Westerpark (park)">Westerpark</a></li><li>H: <a href="/wiki/Flevopark" title="Flevopark">Flevopark</a></li><li>I: <a href="/wiki/Amsterdamse_Bos" title="Amsterdamse Bos">Amsterdamse Bos</a></li><li>J: <a href="/wiki/Amstelpark" title="Amstelpark">Amstelpark</a></li><li>K: <a href="/wiki/Hortus_Botanicus_(Amsterdam)" title="Hortus Botanicus (Amsterdam)">Hortus Botanicus</a></li><li>L: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wertheimerpark&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wertheimerpark (page does not exist)">Wertheimerpark</a></li><li>M: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Luther_Kingpark&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Martin Luther Kingpark (page does not exist)">Martin Luther Kingpark</a></li><li>N: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sloterpark&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sloterpark (page does not exist)">Sloterpark</a></li></ul></div></div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam has many parks, open spaces, and squares throughout the city. The <a href="/wiki/Vondelpark" title="Vondelpark">Vondelpark</a>, the largest park in the city, is located in the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Oud-Zuid" title="Amsterdam Oud-Zuid">Oud-Zuid</a> neighbourhood and is named after the 17th-century Amsterdam author <a href="/wiki/Joost_van_den_Vondel" title="Joost van den Vondel">Joost van den Vondel</a>. Yearly, the park has around 10 million visitors. In the park is an open-air theatre, a playground and several <a href="/wiki/Horeca" title="Horeca">horeca</a> facilities. In the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam-Zuid" title="Amsterdam-Zuid">Zuid</a> borough, is the Beatrixpark, named after <a href="/wiki/Beatrix_of_the_Netherlands" title="Beatrix of the Netherlands">Queen Beatrix</a>. Between Amsterdam and <a href="/wiki/Amstelveen" title="Amstelveen">Amstelveen</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdamse_Bos" title="Amsterdamse Bos">Amsterdamse Bos</a> ("Amsterdam Forest"), the largest recreational area in Amsterdam. Annually, almost 4.5&#160;million people visit the park, which has a size of 1.000 hectares and is approximately three times the size of <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">Central Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Amstelpark" title="Amstelpark">Amstelpark</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam-Zuid" title="Amsterdam-Zuid">Zuid</a> borough houses the Rieker windmill, which dates to 1636. Other parks include the <a href="/wiki/Sarphatipark" title="Sarphatipark">Sarphatipark</a> in the <a href="/wiki/De_Pijp" title="De Pijp">De Pijp</a> neighbourhood, the <a href="/wiki/Oosterpark_(Amsterdam)" title="Oosterpark (Amsterdam)">Oosterpark</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam-Oost" title="Amsterdam-Oost">Oost</a> borough and the <a href="/wiki/Westerpark_(park)" title="Westerpark (park)">Westerpark</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Westerpark_(neighbourhood)" title="Westerpark (neighbourhood)">Westerpark</a> neighbourhood. The city has three beaches: Nemo Beach, Citybeach "Het stenen hoofd" (Silodam) and Blijburg, all located in the Centrum borough.
</p><p>The city has many open squares (<i>plein</i> in Dutch). The namesake of the city as the site of the original dam, <a href="/wiki/Dam_Square" title="Dam Square">Dam Square</a>, is the main city square and has the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Palace_of_Amsterdam" title="Royal Palace of Amsterdam">Royal Palace</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Monument_(Amsterdam)" title="National Monument (Amsterdam)">National Monument</a>. <a href="/wiki/Museumplein" title="Museumplein">Museumplein</a> hosts various museums, including the <a href="/wiki/Rijksmuseum" title="Rijksmuseum">Rijksmuseum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Van_Gogh_Museum" title="Van Gogh Museum">Van Gogh Museum</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stedelijk_Museum_Amsterdam" title="Stedelijk Museum Amsterdam">Stedelijk Museum</a>. Other squares include <a href="/wiki/Rembrandtplein" title="Rembrandtplein">Rembrandtplein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muntplein,_Amsterdam" title="Muntplein, Amsterdam">Muntplein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nieuwmarkt" title="Nieuwmarkt">Nieuwmarkt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leidseplein" title="Leidseplein">Leidseplein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spui_(Amsterdam)" title="Spui (Amsterdam)">Spui</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Waterlooplein" title="Waterlooplein">Waterlooplein</a>. Also, near to Amsterdam is the <a href="/wiki/Nekkeveld_estate" title="Nekkeveld estate">Nekkeveld estate</a> conservation project.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20151120_BeursvanBerlage_002-6972.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/20151120_BeursvanBerlage_002-6972.jpg/250px-20151120_BeursvanBerlage_002-6972.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/20151120_BeursvanBerlage_002-6972.jpg/375px-20151120_BeursvanBerlage_002-6972.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/20151120_BeursvanBerlage_002-6972.jpg/500px-20151120_BeursvanBerlage_002-6972.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="3840" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20151120_BeursvanBerlage_002-6972.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">Amsterdam Stock Exchange</a>, the oldest stock exchange in the world.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zuidas_pano.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Zuidas_pano.jpg/250px-Zuidas_pano.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="85" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Zuidas_pano.jpg/375px-Zuidas_pano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Zuidas_pano.jpg/500px-Zuidas_pano.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5000" data-file-height="1699" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zuidas_pano.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Zuidas" title="Zuidas">Zuidas</a>, the city's main business district.</div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam is the financial and business capital of the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-ez_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ez-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
Amsterdam is ranked fifth best of European cities in which to locate an <a href="/wiki/International_business" title="International business">international business</a>, surpassed by <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eubusiness_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eubusiness-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Many large corporations and banks have their headquarters in Amsterdam, including <a href="/wiki/AkzoNobel" title="AkzoNobel">AkzoNobel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heineken_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Heineken International">Heineken International</a>, <a href="/wiki/ING_Group" title="ING Group">ING Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/ABN_AMRO" title="ABN AMRO">ABN AMRO</a>, <a href="/wiki/TomTom" title="TomTom">TomTom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Lloyd_Group" title="Delta Lloyd Group">Delta Lloyd Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Booking.com" title="Booking.com">Booking.com</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">Philips</a>. <a href="/wiki/KPMG" title="KPMG">KPMG</a> International's global headquarters is located in nearby Amstelveen, where many non-Dutch companies have settled as well, because surrounding communities allow full land ownership, contrary to Amsterdam's land-lease system.
</p><p>Though many small offices are still located on the old canals, companies are increasingly relocating outside the city centre. The <a href="/wiki/Zuidas" title="Zuidas">Zuidas</a> (English: South Axis) has become the new financial and legal hub.<sup id="cite_ref-zuidas_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zuidas-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> The five largest law firms of the Netherlands, a number of Dutch subsidiaries of large consulting firms like <a href="/wiki/Boston_Consulting_Group" title="Boston Consulting Group">Boston Consulting Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Accenture" title="Accenture">Accenture</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(Amsterdam)" title="World Trade Center (Amsterdam)">World Trade Center Amsterdam</a> are also located in Zuidas.
</p><p>There are three other smaller financial districts in Amsterdam. The first is the area surrounding <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Sloterdijk_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Sloterdijk railway station">Amsterdam Sloterdijk railway station</a>, where several newspapers like <i><a href="/wiki/De_Telegraaf" title="De Telegraaf">De Telegraaf</a></i> have their offices.
</p><p>Also, <a href="/wiki/Deloitte" title="Deloitte">Deloitte</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gemeentelijk_Vervoerbedrijf" title="Gemeentelijk Vervoerbedrijf">Gemeentelijk Vervoerbedrijf</a> (municipal public transport company) and the Dutch tax offices (<i>Belastingdienst</i>) are located there. The second <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">Financial District</a> is the area surrounding the <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff_Arena" title="Johan Cruyff Arena">Johan Cruyff Arena</a>. The third is the area surrounding <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Amstel_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Amstel railway station">Amsterdam Amstel railway station</a>. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_and_structures_in_the_world" class="mw-redirect" title="List of tallest buildings and structures in the world">tallest building</a> in Amsterdam, the <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt_Tower" title="Rembrandt Tower">Rembrandt Tower</a>, is situated there, as is the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">Philips</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rembrandtoren_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rembrandtoren-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-philips_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-philips-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Port_of_Amsterdam">Port of Amsterdam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Port of Amsterdam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Amsterdam" title="Port of Amsterdam">Port of Amsterdam</a> is the fourth largest port in Europe, the 38th largest port in the world and the second largest port in the Netherlands by metric tons of cargo. In 2014 the Port of Amsterdam had a cargo throughput of 97,4&#160;million tons of cargo, which was mostly <a href="/wiki/Bulk_cargo" title="Bulk cargo">bulk cargo</a>.
Amsterdam has the biggest cruise port in the Netherlands with more than 150 cruise ships every year.
In 2019 the new lock in IJmuiden will open; the port will then be able to grow to 125&#160;million tonnes in capacity.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">Amsterdam Stock Exchange</a> (AEX), now part of <a href="/wiki/Euronext" title="Euronext">Euronext</a>, is the world's oldest stock exchange and is one of Europe's largest bourses. It is near <a href="/wiki/Dam_Square" title="Dam Square">Dam Square</a> in the city centre.
</p><p>Together with <a href="/wiki/Eindhoven" title="Eindhoven">Eindhoven</a> (<a href="/wiki/BrabantStad#Brainport" class="mw-redirect" title="BrabantStad">Brainport</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> (<a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rotterdam" title="Port of Rotterdam">Seaport</a>), Amsterdam (Airport) forms the foundation of the Dutch economy.<sup id="cite_ref-ref1367203750_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref1367203750-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_tourist_attractions_in_Amsterdam" title="List of tourist attractions in Amsterdam">List of tourist attractions in Amsterdam</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wim_Sonneveld_tour_boat,_Rederij_Lovers,_Amsterdam-9218.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Wim_Sonneveld_tour_boat%2C_Rederij_Lovers%2C_Amsterdam-9218.jpg/220px-Wim_Sonneveld_tour_boat%2C_Rederij_Lovers%2C_Amsterdam-9218.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Wim_Sonneveld_tour_boat%2C_Rederij_Lovers%2C_Amsterdam-9218.jpg/330px-Wim_Sonneveld_tour_boat%2C_Rederij_Lovers%2C_Amsterdam-9218.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Wim_Sonneveld_tour_boat%2C_Rederij_Lovers%2C_Amsterdam-9218.jpg/440px-Wim_Sonneveld_tour_boat%2C_Rederij_Lovers%2C_Amsterdam-9218.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4396" data-file-height="2473" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wim_Sonneveld_tour_boat,_Rederij_Lovers,_Amsterdam-9218.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Boats give tours of the city, such as this one in front of the <a href="/wiki/EYE_Film_Institute_Netherlands" title="EYE Film Institute Netherlands">EYE Film Institute Netherlands</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brug_97_in_de_Spiegelgracht_over_de_Lijnbaansgracht_foto_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Brug_97_in_de_Spiegelgracht_over_de_Lijnbaansgracht_foto_1.jpg/220px-Brug_97_in_de_Spiegelgracht_over_de_Lijnbaansgracht_foto_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Brug_97_in_de_Spiegelgracht_over_de_Lijnbaansgracht_foto_1.jpg/330px-Brug_97_in_de_Spiegelgracht_over_de_Lijnbaansgracht_foto_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Brug_97_in_de_Spiegelgracht_over_de_Lijnbaansgracht_foto_1.jpg/440px-Brug_97_in_de_Spiegelgracht_over_de_Lijnbaansgracht_foto_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brug_97_in_de_Spiegelgracht_over_de_Lijnbaansgracht_foto_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spiegelgracht</div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam is one of the most popular tourist destinations in Europe, receiving more than 4.63&#160;million international visitors annually, this is excluding the 16 million day-trippers visiting the city every year.<sup id="cite_ref-ams2009_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ams2009-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> The number of visitors has been growing steadily over the past decade. This can be attributed to an increasing number of European visitors. Two-thirds of the hotels are located in the city's centre. Hotels with 4 or 5 stars contribute 42% of the total beds available and 41% of the overnight stays in Amsterdam. The room occupation rate was 78% in 2006, up from 70% in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-TourismReport_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TourismReport-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> The majority of tourists (74%) originate from Europe. The largest group of non-European visitors come from the United States, accounting for 14% of the total.<sup id="cite_ref-TourismReport_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TourismReport-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Certain years have a theme in Amsterdam to attract extra tourists. For example, the year 2006 was designated "Rembrandt 400", to celebrate the 400th birthday of <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt van Rijn</a>. Some hotels offer special arrangements or activities during these years. The average number of guests per year staying at the four campsites around the city range from 12,000 to 65,000.<sup id="cite_ref-TourismReport_164-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TourismReport-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="De_Wallen_.28Red-light_district.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="De_Wallen_(Red-light_district)">De Wallen (Red-light district)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: De Wallen (Red-light district)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><span id="Red_light_district"></span>
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/De_Wallen" title="De Wallen">De Wallen</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG/220px-Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG/330px-Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG/440px-Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4280" data-file-height="2811" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Red-light_district_of_Amsterdam_by_day._2012.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/De_Wallen" title="De Wallen">De Wallen</a>, Amsterdam's <a href="/wiki/Red-light_district" title="Red-light district">Red-light district</a>, offers activities such as legal <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_the_Netherlands" title="Prostitution in the Netherlands">prostitution</a> and a number of <a href="/wiki/Coffee_shops" class="mw-redirect" title="Coffee shops">coffee shops</a> that sell <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">cannabis</a>. It is one of the main tourist attractions.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>De Wallen, also known as Walletjes or Rosse Buurt, is a designated area for <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_the_Netherlands" title="Prostitution in the Netherlands">legalised prostitution</a> and is Amsterdam's largest and most well known <a href="/wiki/Red-light_district" title="Red-light district">red-light district</a>. This neighbourhood has become a famous attraction for tourists. It consists of a network of roads and alleys containing several hundred small, one-room apartments rented by <a href="/wiki/Sex_worker" title="Sex worker">sex workers</a> who offer their services from behind a window or glass door, typically illuminated with red lights.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retail">Retail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Retail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Shops in Amsterdam range from large high end department stores such as <a href="/wiki/De_Bijenkorf" title="De Bijenkorf">De Bijenkorf</a> founded in 1870 to small specialty shops. Amsterdam's high-end shops are found in the streets <a href="/wiki/P.C._Hooftstraat" title="P.C. Hooftstraat">P.C. Hooftstraat</a> and <i>Cornelis Schuytstraat</i>, which are located in the vicinity of the <a href="/wiki/Vondelpark" title="Vondelpark">Vondelpark</a>. One of Amsterdam's busiest high streets is the narrow, medieval <a href="/wiki/Kalverstraat" title="Kalverstraat">Kalverstraat</a> in the heart of the city. Other shopping areas include the <i>Negen Straatjes</i> and Haarlemmerdijk and Haarlemmerstraat. <i>Negen Straatjes</i> are nine narrow streets within the <i>Grachtengordel</i>, the concentric canal system of Amsterdam. The Negen Straatjes differ from other shopping districts with the presence of a large diversity of privately owned shops. The Haarlemmerstraat and Haarlemmerdijk were voted best shopping street in the Netherlands in 2011. These streets have as the <i>Negen Straatjes</i> a large diversity of privately owned shops. But as the <i>Negen Straatjes</i> are dominated by fashion stores the Haarlemmerstraat and Haarlemmerdijk offer a very wide variety of all kinds of stores, just to name some specialties: candy and other food related stores, lingerie, sneakers, wedding clothing, interior shops, books, Italian deli's, racing and mountain bikes, skatewear, etc.
</p><p>The city also features a large number of open-air markets such as the <a href="/wiki/Albert_Cuyp_Market" title="Albert Cuyp Market">Albert Cuyp Market</a>, Westerstraat-markt, Ten Katemarkt, and <a href="/wiki/Dappermarkt" title="Dappermarkt">Dappermarkt</a>. Some of these markets are held on a daily basis, like the Albert Cuypmarkt and the Dappermarkt. Others, like the Westerstraatmarkt, are held on a weekly basis.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion">Fashion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Fashion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AmsterdamBikeGirl.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/AmsterdamBikeGirl.png/220px-AmsterdamBikeGirl.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/AmsterdamBikeGirl.png/330px-AmsterdamBikeGirl.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/AmsterdamBikeGirl.png/440px-AmsterdamBikeGirl.png 2x" data-file-width="897" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AmsterdamBikeGirl.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A typically well-attired Amsterdamer waits for a traffic light to change at Muntplein in the heart of Amsterdam.</div></div></div>
<p>Several fashion brands and designers are based in Amsterdam. Brands include <a href="/wiki/G-Star_Raw" title="G-Star Raw">G-star</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/10_feet" title="10 feet">10 feet</a><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Warmenhoven_%26_Venderbos" title="Warmenhoven &amp; Venderbos">Warmenhoven &amp; Venderbos</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and fashion designers include <a href="/wiki/Iris_van_Herpen" title="Iris van Herpen">Iris van Herpen</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mart_Visser" title="Mart Visser">Mart Visser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viktor_%26_Rolf" title="Viktor &amp; Rolf">Viktor &amp; Rolf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marlies_Dekkers" title="Marlies Dekkers">Marlies Dekkers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frans_Molenaar" title="Frans Molenaar">Frans Molenaar</a>. <a href="/wiki/Modeling_agency" title="Modeling agency">Modelling agencies</a> <a href="/wiki/Elite_Model_Management" title="Elite Model Management">Elite Models</a>, Touche models and Tony Jones have opened branches in Amsterdam. Fashion models like <a href="/wiki/Yfke_Sturm" title="Yfke Sturm">Yfke Sturm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doutzen_Kroes" title="Doutzen Kroes">Doutzen Kroes</a> and Kim Noorda started their careers in Amsterdam. Amsterdam has its garment centre in the World Fashion Center. Buildings which formerly housed brothels in the red light district have been converted to ateliers for young fashion designers, AKA eagle fuel.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Fashion photographers <a href="/wiki/Inez_and_Vinoodh" title="Inez and Vinoodh">Inez van Lamsweerde and Vinoodh Matadin</a> were born in Amsterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_rijkmuseum.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Amsterdam_rijkmuseum.JPG/220px-Amsterdam_rijkmuseum.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Amsterdam_rijkmuseum.JPG/330px-Amsterdam_rijkmuseum.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Amsterdam_rijkmuseum.JPG/440px-Amsterdam_rijkmuseum.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2673" data-file-height="1792" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_rijkmuseum.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Rijksmuseum" title="Rijksmuseum">Rijksmuseum</a> houses <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Night_Watch" title="The Night Watch">The Night Watch</a></i>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Van_Gogh_Museum_by_night_Amsterdam_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Van_Gogh_Museum_by_night_Amsterdam_2017.jpg/220px-Van_Gogh_Museum_by_night_Amsterdam_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Van_Gogh_Museum_by_night_Amsterdam_2017.jpg/330px-Van_Gogh_Museum_by_night_Amsterdam_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Van_Gogh_Museum_by_night_Amsterdam_2017.jpg/440px-Van_Gogh_Museum_by_night_Amsterdam_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Van_Gogh_Museum_by_night_Amsterdam_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Van_Gogh_Museum" title="Van Gogh Museum">Van Gogh Museum</a> houses the world's largest collection of <a href="/wiki/Vincent_van_Gogh" title="Vincent van Gogh">Van Gogh</a>'s paintings and letters.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:De_nieuwe_vleugel_van_het_Stedelijk_Museum_Amsterdam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/De_nieuwe_vleugel_van_het_Stedelijk_Museum_Amsterdam.jpg/220px-De_nieuwe_vleugel_van_het_Stedelijk_Museum_Amsterdam.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/De_nieuwe_vleugel_van_het_Stedelijk_Museum_Amsterdam.jpg/330px-De_nieuwe_vleugel_van_het_Stedelijk_Museum_Amsterdam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/De_nieuwe_vleugel_van_het_Stedelijk_Museum_Amsterdam.jpg/440px-De_nieuwe_vleugel_van_het_Stedelijk_Museum_Amsterdam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1675" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:De_nieuwe_vleugel_van_het_Stedelijk_Museum_Amsterdam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Stedelijk_Museum_Amsterdam" title="Stedelijk Museum Amsterdam">Stedelijk Museum Amsterdam</a> is an international museum dedicated to modern and contemporary art and design.</div></div></div>
<p>During the later part of the 16th-century Amsterdam's Rederijkerskamer (<a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_rhetoric" title="Chamber of rhetoric">Chamber of rhetoric</a>) organised contests between different Chambers in the reading of poetry and drama.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> In 1637, <a href="/wiki/Schouwburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Schouwburg">Schouwburg</a>, the first theatre in Amsterdam was built, opening on January 3, 1638.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The first ballet performances in the Netherlands were given in Schouwburg in 1642 with the <i>Ballet of the Five Senses</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> In the 18th century, French theatre became popular. While Amsterdam was under the influence of German music in the 19th century there were few national opera productions;<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> the Hollandse Opera of Amsterdam was built in 1888 for the specific purpose of promoting Dutch opera.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> In the 19th century, popular culture was centred on the Nes area in Amsterdam (mainly <a href="/wiki/Vaudeville" title="Vaudeville">vaudeville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Music_hall" title="Music hall">music-hall</a>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> An improved <a href="/wiki/Metronome" title="Metronome">metronome</a> was invented in 1812 by <a href="/wiki/Dietrich_Nikolaus_Winkel" title="Dietrich Nikolaus Winkel">Dietrich Nikolaus Winkel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Rijksmuseum" title="Rijksmuseum">Rijksmuseum</a> (1885) and <a href="/wiki/Stedelijk_Museum_Amsterdam" title="Stedelijk Museum Amsterdam">Stedelijk Museum</a> (1895) were built and opened.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> In 1888, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Concertgebouw_Orchestra" title="Royal Concertgebouw Orchestra">Concertgebouworkest</a> orchestra was established.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> With the 20th century came cinema, radio and television.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Though most studios are located in <a href="/wiki/Hilversum" title="Hilversum">Hilversum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aalsmeer" title="Aalsmeer">Aalsmeer</a>, Amsterdam's influence on programming is very strong. Many people who work in the television industry live in Amsterdam. Also, the headquarters of the Dutch <a href="/wiki/SBS_6" class="mw-redirect" title="SBS 6">SBS Broadcasting Group</a> is located in Amsterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-sbs6_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sbs6-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The most important museums of Amsterdam are located on the <a href="/wiki/Museumplein" title="Museumplein">Museumplein</a> (Museum Square), located at the southwestern side of the Rijksmuseum. It was created in the last quarter of the 19th century on the grounds of the former <a href="/wiki/Internationale_Koloniale_en_Uitvoerhandel_Tentoonstelling" class="mw-redirect" title="Internationale Koloniale en Uitvoerhandel Tentoonstelling">World's fair</a>. The northeastern part of the square is bordered by the very large Rijksmuseum. In front of the Rijksmuseum on the square itself is a long, rectangular pond. This is transformed into an ice rink in winter.<sup id="cite_ref-ijsbaan_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ijsbaan-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> The northwestern part of the square is bordered by the Van Gogh Museum, Stedelijk Museum, House of Bols Cocktail &amp; Genever Experience and Coster Diamonds. The southwestern border of the Museum Square is the Van Baerlestraat, which is a major thoroughfare in this part of Amsterdam. The Concertgebouw is situated across this street from the square. To the southeast of the square are situated a number of large houses, one of which contains the American consulate. A <a href="/wiki/Multi-storey_car_park" class="mw-redirect" title="Multi-storey car park">parking garage</a> can be found underneath the square, as well as a supermarket. The Museumplein is covered almost entirely with a lawn, except for the northeastern part of the square which is covered with gravel. The current appearance of the square was realised in 1999, when the square was remodelled. The square itself is the most prominent site in Amsterdam for festivals and outdoor concerts, especially in the summer. Plans were made in 2008 to remodel the square again, because many inhabitants of Amsterdam are not happy with its current appearance.<sup id="cite_ref-museumpleinfacelift_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-museumpleinfacelift-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rembrandt.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Rembrandt.JPG/180px-Rembrandt.JPG" decoding="async" width="180" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Rembrandt.JPG/270px-Rembrandt.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Rembrandt.JPG/360px-Rembrandt.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rembrandt.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a> monument on <a href="/wiki/Rembrandtplein" title="Rembrandtplein">Rembrandtplein</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rijksmuseum" title="Rijksmuseum">Rijksmuseum</a> possesses the largest and most important collection of classical <a href="/wiki/Dutch_art" title="Dutch art">Dutch art</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
It opened in 1885. Its collection consists of nearly one million objects.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The artist most associated with Amsterdam is <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a>, whose work, and the work of his pupils, is displayed in the Rijksmuseum. Rembrandt's masterpiece <i><a href="/wiki/The_Night_Watch" title="The Night Watch">The Night Watch</a></i> is one of top pieces of art of the museum.
