It also houses paintings from artists like <a href="/wiki/Bartholomeus_van_der_Helst" title="Bartholomeus van der Helst">Van der Helst</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Vermeer" title="Johannes Vermeer">Vermeer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frans_Hals" title="Frans Hals">Frans Hals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Bol" title="Ferdinand Bol">Ferdinand Bol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aelbert_Cuyp" title="Aelbert Cuyp">Albert Cuyp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacob_van_Ruisdael" title="Jacob van Ruisdael">Jacob van Ruisdael</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paulus_Potter" title="Paulus Potter">Paulus Potter</a>. Aside from paintings, the collection consists of a large variety of <a href="/wiki/Decorative_arts" title="Decorative arts">decorative art</a>. This ranges from <a href="/wiki/Delftware" title="Delftware">Delftware</a> to giant doll-houses from the 17th century. The architect of the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">gothic revival</a> building was P.J.H. Cuypers. The museum underwent a 10-year, 375 million euro renovation starting in 2003. The full collection was reopened to the public on 13 April 2013 and the Rijksmuseum has remained the most visited museum in Amsterdam with 2.2&#160;million visitors in 2016 and 2.16&#160;million in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Van Gogh lived in Amsterdam for a short while and there is a <a href="/wiki/Van_Gogh_Museum" title="Van Gogh Museum">museum dedicated to his work</a>. The museum is housed in one of the few modern buildings in this area of Amsterdam. The building was designed by <a href="/wiki/Gerrit_Rietveld" title="Gerrit Rietveld">Gerrit Rietveld</a>. This building is where the permanent collection is displayed. A new building was added to the museum in 1999. This building, known as the performance wing, was designed by Japanese architect <a href="/wiki/Kisho_Kurokawa" title="Kisho Kurokawa">Kisho Kurokawa</a>. Its purpose is to house temporary exhibitions of the museum.<sup id="cite_ref-vangogh3_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vangogh3-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> Some of Van Gogh's most famous paintings, like <i><a href="/wiki/The_Potato_Eaters" title="The Potato Eaters">The Potato Eaters</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Sunflowers_(series_of_paintings)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunflowers (series of paintings)">Sunflowers</a></i>, are in the collection.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> The Van Gogh museum is the second most visited museum in Amsterdam, not far behind the Rijksmuseum in terms of the number of visits, being approximately 2.1&#160;million in 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> for example.
</p><p>Next to the Van Gogh museum stands the <a href="/wiki/Stedelijk_Museum_Amsterdam" title="Stedelijk Museum Amsterdam">Stedelijk Museum</a>. This is Amsterdam's most important museum of modern art. The museum is as old as the square it borders and was opened in 1895. The permanent collection consists of works of art from artists like <a href="/wiki/Piet_Mondrian" title="Piet Mondrian">Piet Mondriaan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karel_Appel" title="Karel Appel">Karel Appel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kazimir_Malevich" title="Kazimir Malevich">Kazimir Malevich</a>. After renovations lasting several years the museum opened in September 2012 with a new composite extension that has been called 'The Bathtub' due to its resemblance to one.
</p><p>Amsterdam contains many other museums throughout the city. They range from small museums such as the <a href="/wiki/Verzetsmuseum" title="Verzetsmuseum">Verzetsmuseum</a> (Resistance Museum), the <a href="/wiki/Anne_Frank_House" title="Anne Frank House">Anne Frank House</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt_House_Museum" title="Rembrandt House Museum">Rembrandt House Museum</a>, to the very large, like the <a href="/wiki/Tropenmuseum" title="Tropenmuseum">Tropenmuseum</a> (Museum of the Tropics), <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Museum" title="Amsterdam Museum">Amsterdam Museum</a> (formerly known as Amsterdam Historical Museum), <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Amsterdam" title="Hermitage Amsterdam">Hermitage Amsterdam</a> (a dependency of the <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Museum" title="Hermitage Museum">Hermitage Museum</a> in Saint Petersburg) and the <a href="/wiki/Joods_Historisch_Museum" title="Joods Historisch Museum">Joods Historisch Museum</a> (Jewish Historical Museum). The modern-styled <a href="/wiki/NEMO_(museum)" title="NEMO (museum)">Nemo</a> is dedicated to child-friendly science exhibitions.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_songs_about_Amsterdam" title="List of songs about Amsterdam">List of songs about Amsterdam</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coldplay_perform_%22Adventure_of_a_Lifetime%22,_Amsterdam_Arena,_June_2016_(5).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Coldplay_perform_%22Adventure_of_a_Lifetime%22%2C_Amsterdam_Arena%2C_June_2016_%285%29.jpg/220px-Coldplay_perform_%22Adventure_of_a_Lifetime%22%2C_Amsterdam_Arena%2C_June_2016_%285%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Coldplay_perform_%22Adventure_of_a_Lifetime%22%2C_Amsterdam_Arena%2C_June_2016_%285%29.jpg/330px-Coldplay_perform_%22Adventure_of_a_Lifetime%22%2C_Amsterdam_Arena%2C_June_2016_%285%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Coldplay_perform_%22Adventure_of_a_Lifetime%22%2C_Amsterdam_Arena%2C_June_2016_%285%29.jpg/440px-Coldplay_perform_%22Adventure_of_a_Lifetime%22%2C_Amsterdam_Arena%2C_June_2016_%285%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1406" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coldplay_perform_%22Adventure_of_a_Lifetime%22,_Amsterdam_Arena,_June_2016_(5).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a> performing at the <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff_Arena" title="Johan Cruyff Arena">Amsterdam Arena</a>, 2016.</div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam's musical culture includes a large collection of songs which treat the city nostalgically and lovingly. The 1949 song "Aan de Amsterdamse grachten" ("On the canals of Amsterdam") was performed and recorded by many artists, including <a href="/wiki/John_Kraaijkamp_Sr." title="John Kraaijkamp Sr.">John Kraaijkamp Sr.</a>; the best-known version is probably that by <a href="/wiki/Wim_Sonneveld" title="Wim Sonneveld">Wim Sonneveld</a> (1962). In the 1950s <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Jordaan" title="Johnny Jordaan">Johnny Jordaan</a> rose to fame with "<a href="/wiki/Geef_mij_maar_Amsterdam" title="Geef mij maar Amsterdam">Geef mij maar Amsterdam</a>" ("I prefer Amsterdam"), which praises the city above all others (explicitly Paris); Jordaan sang especially about his own neighbourhood, the <a href="/wiki/Jordaan" title="Jordaan">Jordaan</a> ("Bij ons in de Jordaan"). Colleagues and contemporaries of Johnny include <a href="/wiki/Tante_Leen" title="Tante Leen">Tante Leen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manke_Nelis" title="Manke Nelis">Manke Nelis</a>. Other notable Amsterdam songs are "<a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_(Jacques_Brel_song)" title="Amsterdam (Jacques Brel song)">Amsterdam</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Brel" title="Jacques Brel">Jacques Brel</a> (1964) and "Deze Stad" by <a href="/wiki/De_Dijk" title="De Dijk">De Dijk</a> (1989).<sup id="cite_ref-lijflied_finale_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lijflied_finale-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> A 2011 poll by Amsterdam newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Het_Parool" title="Het Parool">Het Parool</a></i> that Trio Bier's "Oude Wolf" was voted "Amsterdams lijflied".<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Notable Amsterdam bands from the modern era include the <a href="/wiki/Osdorp_Posse" title="Osdorp Posse">Osdorp Posse</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Ex_(band)" title="The Ex (band)">The Ex</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/AFAS_Live" title="AFAS Live">AFAS Live</a> (formerly known as the Heineken Music Hall) is a concert hall located near the <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff_Arena" title="Johan Cruyff Arena">Johan Cruyff Arena</a> (known as the Amsterdam Arena until 2018). Its main purpose is to serve as a podium for pop concerts for big audiences. Many famous international artists have performed there. Two other notable venues, <a href="/wiki/Paradiso_(Amsterdam)" title="Paradiso (Amsterdam)">Paradiso</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Melkweg" title="Melkweg">Melkweg</a> are located near the <a href="/wiki/Leidseplein" title="Leidseplein">Leidseplein</a>. Both focus on broad programming, ranging from <a href="/wiki/Indie_rock" title="Indie rock">indie rock</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">R&amp;B</a>, and other popular genres. Other more subcultural music venues are <a href="/wiki/OCCII" title="OCCII">OCCII</a>, <a href="/wiki/OT301" title="OT301">OT301</a>, De Nieuwe Anita, Winston Kingdom and Zaal 100. <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">Jazz</a> has a strong following in Amsterdam, with the <a href="/wiki/Bimhuis" title="Bimhuis">Bimhuis</a> being the premier venue. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Ziggo_Dome" title="Ziggo Dome">Ziggo Dome</a> was opened, also near Amsterdam Arena, a state-of-the-art indoor music arena.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/AFAS_Live" title="AFAS Live">AFAS Live</a> is also host to many <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">electronic dance music</a> festivals, alongside many other venues. <a href="/wiki/Armin_van_Buuren" title="Armin van Buuren">Armin van Buuren</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tiesto" class="mw-redirect" title="Tiesto">Tiesto</a>, some of the world's leading <a href="/wiki/Trance_music" title="Trance music">Trance</a> DJ's hail from the Netherlands and perform frequently in Amsterdam. Each year in October, the city hosts the Amsterdam Dance Event (ADE) which is one of the leading electronic music conferences and one of the biggest club festivals for electronic music in the world, attracting over 350,000 visitors each year.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> Another popular dance festival is 5daysoff, which takes place in the venues <a href="/wiki/Paradiso_(Amsterdam)" title="Paradiso (Amsterdam)">Paradiso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melkweg" title="Melkweg">Melkweg</a>. In summer time there are several big outdoor dance parties in or nearby Amsterdam, such as Awakenings, <a href="/wiki/Dance_Valley" title="Dance Valley">Dance Valley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mysteryland" title="Mysteryland">Mystery Land</a>, Loveland, A Day at the Park, Welcome to the Future, and Valtifest.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Concertgebouw.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Amsterdam_Concertgebouw.jpg/220px-Amsterdam_Concertgebouw.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Amsterdam_Concertgebouw.jpg/330px-Amsterdam_Concertgebouw.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Amsterdam_Concertgebouw.jpg/440px-Amsterdam_Concertgebouw.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1363" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Concertgebouw.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Concertgebouw" title="Concertgebouw">Concertgebouw</a> or Royal Concert Hall houses performances of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Concertgebouw_Orchestra" title="Royal Concertgebouw Orchestra">Royal Concertgebouw Orchestra</a> and other musical events.</div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam has a world-class symphony orchestra, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Concertgebouw_Orchestra" title="Royal Concertgebouw Orchestra">Royal Concertgebouw Orchestra</a>. Their home is the <a href="/wiki/Concertgebouw" title="Concertgebouw">Concertgebouw</a>, which is across the Van Baerlestraat from the Museum Square. It is considered by critics to be a <a href="/wiki/List_of_concert_halls" title="List of concert halls">concert hall</a> with some of the best <a href="/wiki/Acoustics" title="Acoustics">acoustics</a> in the world. The building contains three halls, Grote Zaal, Kleine Zaal, and Spiegelzaal. Some nine hundred concerts and other events per year take place in the Concertgebouw, for a public of over 700,000, making it one of the most-visited concert halls in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> The opera house of Amsterdam is situated adjacent to the city hall. Therefore, the two buildings combined are often called the <a href="/wiki/Stopera" title="Stopera">Stopera</a>, (a word originally coined by protesters against it very construction: <i>Stop the Opera[-house]</i>). This huge modern complex, opened in 1986, lies in the former Jewish neighbourhood at <i>Waterlooplein</i> next to the river <a href="/wiki/Amstel" title="Amstel">Amstel</a>. The <i>Stopera</i> is the homebase of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_National_Opera" title="Dutch National Opera">Dutch National Opera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_National_Ballet" title="Dutch National Ballet">Dutch National Ballet</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Holland_Symfonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Holland Symfonia">Holland Symfonia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Muziekgebouw_aan_%27t_IJ" title="Muziekgebouw aan &#39;t IJ">Muziekgebouw aan 't IJ</a> is a concert hall, which is situated in the <a href="/wiki/IJ_(Amsterdam)" title="IJ (Amsterdam)">IJ</a> near the central station. Its concerts perform mostly <a href="/wiki/20th-century_classical_music" title="20th-century classical music">modern classical music</a>. Located adjacent to it, is the <i><a href="/wiki/Bimhuis" title="Bimhuis">Bimhuis</a></i>, a concert hall for improvised and <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">Jazz</a> music.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Performing arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadsschouwburg_amsterdam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Stadsschouwburg_amsterdam.jpg/220px-Stadsschouwburg_amsterdam.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Stadsschouwburg_amsterdam.jpg/330px-Stadsschouwburg_amsterdam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Stadsschouwburg_amsterdam.jpg/440px-Stadsschouwburg_amsterdam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadsschouwburg_amsterdam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Stadsschouwburg" title="Stadsschouwburg">Stadsschouwburg</a>, Amsterdam's best known theatre.</div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam has three main theatre buildings.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Stadsschouwburg" title="Stadsschouwburg">Stadsschouwburg</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Leidseplein" title="Leidseplein">Leidseplein</a> is the home base of <a href="/wiki/Toneelgroep_Amsterdam" title="Toneelgroep Amsterdam">Toneelgroep Amsterdam</a>. The current building dates from 1894. Most plays are performed in the Grote Zaal (Great Hall). The normal programme of events encompasses all sorts of theatrical forms. The Stadsschouwburg is currently being renovated and expanded. The third theatre space, to be operated jointly with next door <a href="/wiki/Melkweg" title="Melkweg">Melkweg</a>, will open in late 2009 or early 2010.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Stopera" title="Stopera">Dutch National Opera and Ballet</a> (formerly known as <i>Het Muziektheater</i>), dating from 1986, is the principal opera house and home to <a href="/wiki/Dutch_National_Opera" title="Dutch National Opera">Dutch National Opera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_National_Ballet" title="Dutch National Ballet">Dutch National Ballet</a>. <a href="/wiki/Carr%C3%A9_Theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Carré Theatre">Royal Theatre Carré</a> was built as a permanent circus theatre in 1887 and is currently mainly used for musicals, <a href="/wiki/Cabaret" title="Cabaret">cabaret</a> performances and pop concerts.
</p><p>The recently re-opened DeLaMar Theater houses the more commercial plays and musicals. A new theatre has also moved into Amsterdam scene in 2014, joining other established venues: Theater Amsterdam is situated in the west part of Amsterdam, on the Danzigerkade. It is housed in a modern building with a panoramic view over the harbour. The theatre is the first ever purpose-built venue to showcase a single play entitled ANNE, the play based on Anne Frank's life.
</p><p>On the east side of town there is a small theatre in a converted bath house, the <a href="/wiki/Badhuistheater" title="Badhuistheater">Badhuistheater</a>. The theatre often has English programming.
</p><p>The Netherlands has a tradition of cabaret or <i>kleinkunst</i>, which combines music, storytelling, commentary, theatre and comedy. Cabaret dates back to the 1930s and artists like <a href="/wiki/Wim_Kan" title="Wim Kan">Wim Kan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wim_Sonneveld" title="Wim Sonneveld">Wim Sonneveld</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toon_Hermans" title="Toon Hermans">Toon Hermans</a> were pioneers of this form of art in the Netherlands. In Amsterdam is the Kleinkunstacademie (English: Cabaret Academy). Contemporary popular artists are <a href="/wiki/Youp_van_%27t_Hek" title="Youp van &#39;t Hek">Youp van 't Hek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freek_de_Jonge" title="Freek de Jonge">Freek de Jonge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herman_Finkers" title="Herman Finkers">Herman Finkers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hans_Teeuwen" title="Hans Teeuwen">Hans Teeuwen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theo_Maassen" title="Theo Maassen">Theo Maassen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herman_van_Veen" title="Herman van Veen">Herman van Veen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Najib_Amhali" title="Najib Amhali">Najib Amhali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raoul_Heertje" title="Raoul Heertje">Raoul Heertje</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B6rgen_Raymann" title="Jörgen Raymann">Jörgen Raymann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brigitte_Kaandorp" title="Brigitte Kaandorp">Brigitte Kaandorp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Comedytrain" class="mw-redirect" title="Comedytrain">Comedytrain</a>. The English spoken comedy scene was established with the founding of <a href="/wiki/Boom_Chicago" title="Boom Chicago">Boom Chicago</a> in 1993. They have their own theatre at Leidseplein.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nightlife">Nightlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Nightlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:DeWolff_Paradiso.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/DeWolff_Paradiso.jpg/200px-DeWolff_Paradiso.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/DeWolff_Paradiso.jpg/300px-DeWolff_Paradiso.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/DeWolff_Paradiso.jpg/400px-DeWolff_Paradiso.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7360" data-file-height="4912" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">DeWolff performing at <a href="/wiki/Paradiso_(Amsterdam)" title="Paradiso (Amsterdam)">Paradiso</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Magere_Brug.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Amsterdam_Magere_Brug.jpg/200px-Amsterdam_Magere_Brug.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Amsterdam_Magere_Brug.jpg/300px-Amsterdam_Magere_Brug.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Amsterdam_Magere_Brug.jpg/400px-Amsterdam_Magere_Brug.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1065" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">The <a href="/wiki/Magere_Brug" title="Magere Brug">Magere Brug</a> or "Skinny Bridge" over the <a href="/wiki/Amstel" title="Amstel">Amstel</a> at night.</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam is famous for its vibrant and diverse nightlife. Amsterdam has many <i><a href="/wiki/Bar_(establishment)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bar (establishment)">cafés</a></i> (bars). They range from large and modern to small and cozy. The typical <i>Bruine Kroeg</i> (brown <i>café</i>) breathe a more old fashioned atmosphere with dimmed lights, candles, and somewhat older clientele. Most <i>cafés</i> have terraces in summertime. A common sight on the Leidseplein during summer is a square full of terraces packed with people drinking beer or wine. Many restaurants can be found in Amsterdam as well. Since Amsterdam is a multicultural city, a lot of different ethnic restaurants can be found. Restaurants range from being rather luxurious and expensive to being ordinary and affordable. Amsterdam also possesses many <a href="/wiki/Discoth%C3%A8que" class="mw-redirect" title="Discothèque">discothèques</a>. The two main nightlife areas for tourists are the <a href="/wiki/Leidseplein" title="Leidseplein">Leidseplein</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Rembrandtplein" title="Rembrandtplein">Rembrandtplein</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Paradiso_(Amsterdam)" title="Paradiso (Amsterdam)">Paradiso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melkweg" title="Melkweg">Melkweg</a> and Sugar Factory are cultural centres, which turn into discothèques on some nights. Examples of discothèques near the Rembrandtplein are the Escape, Air, John Doe and Club Abe. Also noteworthy are Panama, Hotel Arena (East), TrouwAmsterdam and Studio 80. <a href="/wiki/Bimhuis" title="Bimhuis">Bimhuis</a> located near the Central Station, with its rich programming hosting the best in the field is considered one of the best jazz clubs in the world. The Reguliersdwarsstraat is the main street for the <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> community and nightlife.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen%27s_Day_in_Amsterdam_2013_(8697415382).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Queen%27s_Day_in_Amsterdam_2013_%288697415382%29.jpg/200px-Queen%27s_Day_in_Amsterdam_2013_%288697415382%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Queen%27s_Day_in_Amsterdam_2013_%288697415382%29.jpg/300px-Queen%27s_Day_in_Amsterdam_2013_%288697415382%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Queen%27s_Day_in_Amsterdam_2013_%288697415382%29.jpg/400px-Queen%27s_Day_in_Amsterdam_2013_%288697415382%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Koningsdag" title="Koningsdag">Queen's Day</a> in Amsterdam on 2013.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam%27s_Canals.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Amsterdam%27s_Canals.jpg/200px-Amsterdam%27s_Canals.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Amsterdam%27s_Canals.jpg/300px-Amsterdam%27s_Canals.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Amsterdam%27s_Canals.jpg/400px-Amsterdam%27s_Canals.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="540" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">People dressed in orange on the <a href="/wiki/Canals_of_Amsterdam" title="Canals of Amsterdam">canals of Amsterdam</a> in 2010 during <a href="/wiki/Koningsdag" title="Koningsdag">Koningsdag</a> or King's Day.</div></div></div></div></div> 
<p>In 2008, there were 140 festivals and events in Amsterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-festivals_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-festivals-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Famous festivals and events in Amsterdam include: <i><a href="/wiki/Koningsdag" title="Koningsdag">Koningsdag</a></i> (which was named <i>Koninginnedag</i> until the crowning of King Willem-Alexander in 2013) (King's Day – Queen's Day); the <a href="/wiki/Holland_Festival" title="Holland Festival">Holland Festival</a> for the performing arts; the yearly <a href="/wiki/Prinsengrachtconcert" title="Prinsengrachtconcert">Prinsengrachtconcert</a> (classical concerto on the Prinsen canal) in August; the '<a href="/wiki/Stille_Omgang" title="Stille Omgang">Stille Omgang</a>' (a silent Roman Catholic evening procession held every March); <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Gay_Pride" title="Amsterdam Gay Pride">Amsterdam Gay Pride</a>; The <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_Cup" title="Cannabis Cup">Cannabis Cup</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Uitmarkt" title="Uitmarkt">Uitmarkt</a>. On Koninginnedag—that was held each year on 30 April—hundreds of thousands of people travel to Amsterdam to celebrate with the city's residents and Koningsdag is held on 27 April. The entire city becomes overcrowded with people buying products from the <i>freemarket,</i> or visiting one of the many music concerts.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Gay_Pride_2013_boat_no37_Hot_Spot_Cafe_pic7.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Amsterdam_Gay_Pride_2013_boat_no37_Hot_Spot_Cafe_pic7.JPG/220px-Amsterdam_Gay_Pride_2013_boat_no37_Hot_Spot_Cafe_pic7.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Amsterdam_Gay_Pride_2013_boat_no37_Hot_Spot_Cafe_pic7.JPG/330px-Amsterdam_Gay_Pride_2013_boat_no37_Hot_Spot_Cafe_pic7.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Amsterdam_Gay_Pride_2013_boat_no37_Hot_Spot_Cafe_pic7.JPG/440px-Amsterdam_Gay_Pride_2013_boat_no37_Hot_Spot_Cafe_pic7.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4126" data-file-height="3100" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Gay_Pride_2013_boat_no37_Hot_Spot_Cafe_pic7.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of the decorated boats participating in the 2013 Canal Parade of the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Gay_Pride" title="Amsterdam Gay Pride">Amsterdam Gay Pride</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The yearly Holland Festival attracts international artists and visitors from all over Europe. <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Gay_Pride" title="Amsterdam Gay Pride">Amsterdam Gay Pride</a> is a yearly local LGBT parade of boats in Amsterdam's canals, held on the first Saturday in August.<sup id="cite_ref-gaypride_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gaypride-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> The annual Uitmarkt is a three-day cultural event at the start of the cultural season in late August. It offers previews of many different artists, such as musicians and poets, who perform on <a href="/wiki/Podium" title="Podium">podia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uitmarkt_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uitmarkt-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Amsterdam is home of the <i><a href="/wiki/Eredivisie" title="Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a></i> football club <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">AFC Ajax</a>. The stadium <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff_Arena" title="Johan Cruyff Arena">Johan Cruyff Arena</a> is the home of Ajax. It is located in the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Zuidoost" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Zuidoost">south-east</a> of the city next to the new <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Bijlmer_ArenA_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Bijlmer ArenA railway station">Amsterdam Bijlmer ArenA railway station</a>. Before moving to their current location in 1996, Ajax played their regular matches in <a href="/wiki/De_Meer_Stadion" title="De Meer Stadion">De Meer Stadion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>
In 1928, Amsterdam hosted the <a href="/wiki/1928_Summer_Olympics" title="1928 Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Amsterdam)" title="Olympic Stadium (Amsterdam)">Olympic Stadium</a> built for the occasion has been completely restored and is now used for cultural and sporting events, such as the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Marathon" title="Amsterdam Marathon">Amsterdam Marathon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> In 1920, Amsterdam assisted in hosting some of the <a href="/wiki/Sailing_at_the_1920_Summer_Olympics" title="Sailing at the 1920 Summer Olympics">sailing</a> events for the <a href="/wiki/1920_Summer_Olympics" title="1920 Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics</a> held in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>, Belgium by hosting events at <a href="/wiki/IJ_(Amsterdam)" title="IJ (Amsterdam)">Buiten Y</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Feyenoord_tegen_Ajax_1-0._Nummer_26_Israel_in_duel_met_Cruyff.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Feyenoord_tegen_Ajax_1-0._Nummer_26_Israel_in_duel_met_Cruyff.jpg/220px-Feyenoord_tegen_Ajax_1-0._Nummer_26_Israel_in_duel_met_Cruyff.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Feyenoord_tegen_Ajax_1-0._Nummer_26_Israel_in_duel_met_Cruyff.jpg/330px-Feyenoord_tegen_Ajax_1-0._Nummer_26_Israel_in_duel_met_Cruyff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Feyenoord_tegen_Ajax_1-0._Nummer_26_Israel_in_duel_met_Cruyff.jpg/440px-Feyenoord_tegen_Ajax_1-0._Nummer_26_Israel_in_duel_met_Cruyff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2406" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Feyenoord_tegen_Ajax_1-0._Nummer_26_Israel_in_duel_met_Cruyff.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">AFC Ajax</a> player <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff" title="Johan Cruyff">Johan Cruyff</a>, 1967.</div></div></div>
<p>The city holds the <a href="/wiki/Dam_tot_Damloop" title="Dam tot Damloop">Dam to Dam Run</a>, a 16-kilometre (10&#160;mi) race from Amsterdam to <a href="/wiki/Zaandam" title="Zaandam">Zaandam</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Marathon" title="Amsterdam Marathon">Amsterdam Marathon</a>. The ice hockey team <a href="/wiki/Amstel_Tijgers" class="mw-redirect" title="Amstel Tijgers">Amstel Tijgers</a> play in the <a href="/wiki/Jaap_Eden" title="Jaap Eden">Jaap Eden</a> ice rink. The team competes in the Dutch ice hockey premier league. <a href="/wiki/Long_track_speed_skating" title="Long track speed skating">Speed skating</a> championships have been held on the 400-metre lane of this ice rink.
</p><p>Amsterdam holds two <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> franchises: the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Crusaders" title="Amsterdam Crusaders">Amsterdam Crusaders</a> and the Amsterdam Panthers. The <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Pirates" title="Amsterdam Pirates">Amsterdam Pirates</a> baseball team competes in the <a href="/wiki/Honkbal_Hoofdklasse" title="Honkbal Hoofdklasse">Dutch Major League</a>. There are three <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a> teams: Amsterdam, Pinoké and Hurley, who play their matches around the <a href="/wiki/Wagener_Stadium" title="Wagener Stadium">Wagener Stadium</a> in the nearby city of <a href="/wiki/Amstelveen" title="Amstelveen">Amstelveen</a>. The basketball team <a href="/wiki/MyGuide_Amsterdam" class="mw-redirect" title="MyGuide Amsterdam">MyGuide Amsterdam</a> competes in the Dutch premier division and play their games in the Sporthallen Zuid.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There is one rugby club in Amsterdam, which also hosts sports training classes such as RTC (Rugby Talenten Centrum or Rugby Talent Centre) and the National Rugby stadium.
</p><p>Since 1999 the city of Amsterdam honours the best sportsmen and women at the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Sportsman_of_the_year" title="Amsterdam Sportsman of the year">Amsterdam Sports Awards</a>. Boxer <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Joval" title="Raymond Joval">Raymond Joval</a> and field hockey midfielder <a href="/wiki/Carole_Thate" title="Carole Thate">Carole Thate</a> were the first to receive the awards, in 1999.
</p><p>Amsterdam hosted the <a href="/wiki/World_Gymnaestrada" title="World Gymnaestrada">World Gymnaestrada</a> in 1991 and will do so again in 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Amsterdam" title="Government of Amsterdam">Government of Amsterdam</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Femke_Halsema-roel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Femke_Halsema-roel.jpg/200px-Femke_Halsema-roel.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Femke_Halsema-roel.jpg/300px-Femke_Halsema-roel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Femke_Halsema-roel.jpg/400px-Femke_Halsema-roel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1245" data-file-height="1279" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Femke_Halsema-roel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Femke_Halsema" title="Femke Halsema">Femke Halsema</a> has been <a href="/wiki/Burgemeester" class="mw-redirect" title="Burgemeester">Mayor</a> of Amsterdam since 2018.</div></div></div> 
<p>The city of Amsterdam is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_of_the_Netherlands" title="List of municipalities of the Netherlands">municipality</a> under the Dutch Municipalities Act. It is governed by a directly elected <a href="/wiki/Municipal_council_(Netherlands)" title="Municipal council (Netherlands)">municipal council</a>, a <a href="/wiki/College_van_burgemeester_en_wethouders" title="College van burgemeester en wethouders">municipal executive board</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Burgemeester" class="mw-redirect" title="Burgemeester">mayor</a>. Since 1981, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_of_the_Netherlands" title="List of municipalities of the Netherlands">municipality</a> of Amsterdam has gradually been divided into semi-autonomous <a href="/wiki/Boroughs_of_Amsterdam" title="Boroughs of Amsterdam">boroughs</a>, called <i>stadsdelen</i> or 'districts'. Over time, a total of 15 boroughs were created. In May 2010, under a major reform, the number of <a href="/wiki/Boroughs_of_Amsterdam" title="Boroughs of Amsterdam">Amsterdam boroughs</a> was reduced to eight: <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam-Centrum" title="Amsterdam-Centrum">Amsterdam-Centrum</a> covering the city centre including the <a href="/wiki/Canals_of_Amsterdam" title="Canals of Amsterdam">canal belt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam-Noord" title="Amsterdam-Noord">Amsterdam-Noord</a> consisting of the neighbourhoods north of the <a href="/wiki/IJ_(Amsterdam)" title="IJ (Amsterdam)">IJ lake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam-Oost" title="Amsterdam-Oost">Amsterdam-Oost</a> in the east, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam-Zuid" title="Amsterdam-Zuid">Amsterdam-Zuid</a> in the south, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam-West" title="Amsterdam-West">Amsterdam-West</a> in the west, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Nieuw-West" title="Amsterdam Nieuw-West">Amsterdam Nieuw-West</a> in the far west, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Zuidoost" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Zuidoost">Amsterdam Zuidoost</a> in the southeast, and <a href="/wiki/Westpoort_(Amsterdam)" class="mw-redirect" title="Westpoort (Amsterdam)">Westpoort</a> covering the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Amsterdam" title="Port of Amsterdam">Port of Amsterdam</a> area.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_government">City government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: City government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Boroughs_of_Amsterdam" title="Boroughs of Amsterdam">Boroughs of Amsterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipal_council_(Netherlands)" title="Municipal council (Netherlands)">Municipal council (Netherlands)</a></div>
<p>As with all Dutch municipalities, Amsterdam is governed by a directly elected <a href="/wiki/Municipal_council_(Netherlands)" title="Municipal council (Netherlands)">municipal council</a>, a <a href="/wiki/College_van_burgemeester_en_wethouders" title="College van burgemeester en wethouders">municipal executive board</a> and a government appointed<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Burgemeester" class="mw-redirect" title="Burgemeester">mayor</a> (<i>burgemeester</i>). The mayor is a member of the municipal executive board, but also has individual responsibilies in maintaining public order. On 27 June 2018 <a href="/wiki/Femke_Halsema" title="Femke Halsema">Femke Halsema</a> (former member of <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_(Netherlands)" title="House of Representatives (Netherlands)">House of Representatives</a> for <a href="/wiki/GroenLinks" title="GroenLinks">GroenLinks</a> from 1998 to 2011) was appointed as the first woman to be <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Amsterdam" title="List of mayors of Amsterdam">Mayor of Amsterdam</a> by the <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Commissioner" class="mw-redirect" title="King&#39;s Commissioner">King's Commissioner</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Holland" title="North Holland">North Holland</a> for a six-year term after being nominated by the Amsterdam <a href="/wiki/Municipal_council_(Netherlands)" title="Municipal council (Netherlands)">municipal council</a>.  and began serving a six-year term on 12 July 2018. She replaces <a href="/wiki/Eberhard_van_der_Laan" title="Eberhard van der Laan">Eberhard van der Laan</a> (<a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Netherlands)" title="Labour Party (Netherlands)">Labour Party</a>) who was the Mayor of Amsterdam from 2010 until his death in October 2017. After the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_municipal_elections,_2014" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch municipal elections, 2014">2014 municipal council elections</a>, a governing majority of <a href="/wiki/Democrats_66" title="Democrats 66">D66</a>, <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_for_Freedom_and_Democracy" title="People&#39;s Party for Freedom and Democracy">VVD</a> and <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_(Netherlands)" title="Socialist Party (Netherlands)">SP</a> was formed – the first coalition without the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Netherlands)" title="Labour Party (Netherlands)">Labour Party</a> since <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Next to the <a href="/wiki/Burgemeester" class="mw-redirect" title="Burgemeester">Mayor</a>, the <a href="/wiki/College_van_burgemeester_en_wethouders" title="College van burgemeester en wethouders">municipal executive board</a> consists of eight <i>wethouders</i> ('alderpersons') appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Municipal_council_(Netherlands)" title="Municipal council (Netherlands)">municipal council</a>: four <a href="/wiki/Democrats_66" title="Democrats 66">D66</a> alderpersons, two <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_for_Freedom_and_Democracy" title="People&#39;s Party for Freedom and Democracy">VVD</a> alderpersons and two <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_(Netherlands)" title="Socialist Party (Netherlands)">SP</a> alderpersons.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 18 September 2017 it was announced by <a href="/wiki/Eberhard_van_der_Laan" title="Eberhard van der Laan">Eberhard van der Laan</a> in an open letter to Amsterdam citizens that <a href="/wiki/Kajsa_Ollongren" title="Kajsa Ollongren">Kajsa Ollongren</a> would take up his office as acting Mayor of Amsterdam with immediate effect due to ill health.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Ollongren was succeeded as acting Mayor by Eric van der Burg on 26 October 2017 and by <a href="/wiki/Jozias_van_Aartsen" title="Jozias van Aartsen">Jozias van Aartsen</a> on 4 December 2017.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdamse_stadsdelen_2010.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Amsterdamse_stadsdelen_2010.png/250px-Amsterdamse_stadsdelen_2010.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Amsterdamse_stadsdelen_2010.png/375px-Amsterdamse_stadsdelen_2010.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Amsterdamse_stadsdelen_2010.png/500px-Amsterdamse_stadsdelen_2010.png 2x" data-file-width="654" data-file-height="505" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdamse_stadsdelen_2010.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Boroughs_of_Amsterdam" title="Boroughs of Amsterdam">Boroughs of Amsterdam</a></div></div></div>
<p>Unlike most other Dutch municipalities, Amsterdam is subdivided into eight <a href="/wiki/Boroughs_of_Amsterdam" title="Boroughs of Amsterdam">boroughs</a>, called <i>stadsdelen</i> or 'districts', a system that was implemented gradually in the 1980s to improve local governance. The <a href="/wiki/Boroughs_of_Amsterdam" title="Boroughs of Amsterdam">boroughs</a> are responsible for many activities that had previously been run by the central city. In 2010, the number of <a href="/wiki/Boroughs_of_Amsterdam" title="Boroughs of Amsterdam">Amsterdam boroughs</a> reached fifteen. Fourteen of those had their own district council (<i>deelraad</i>), elected by a popular vote. The fifteenth, <a href="/wiki/Westpoort" title="Westpoort">Westpoort</a>, covers the harbour of Amsterdam and had very few residents. Therefore, it was governed by the central municipal council.
</p><p>Under the borough system, municipal decisions are made at borough level, except for those affairs pertaining to the whole city such as major infrastructure projects, which are the jurisdiction of the central municipal authorities. In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Boroughs_of_Amsterdam" title="Boroughs of Amsterdam">borough</a> system was restructured, in which many smaller boroughs merged into larger boroughs. In 2014, under a reform of the Dutch Municipalities Act, the <a href="/wiki/Boroughs_of_Amsterdam" title="Boroughs of Amsterdam">Amsterdam boroughs</a> lost much of their autonomous status, as their district councils were abolished.
</p><p>The municipal council of Amsterdam voted to maintain the borough system by replacing the district councils with smaller, but still directly elected district committees (<i>bestuurscommissies</i>). Under a municipal ordinance, the new district committees were granted responsibilities through delegation of regulatory and executive powers by the central municipal council.
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Amstel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Amsterdam_Amstel.jpg/800px-Amsterdam_Amstel.jpg" decoding="async" width="800" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Amsterdam_Amstel.jpg/1200px-Amsterdam_Amstel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Amsterdam_Amstel.jpg/1600px-Amsterdam_Amstel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5272" data-file-height="1361" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Amstel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center>View of the <a href="/wiki/Stopera" title="Stopera">Stopera</a> (left, behind the <a href="/wiki/Blauwbrug" title="Blauwbrug">blue bridge</a>), where the Amsterdam city hall and opera house are located, and the <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Amsterdam" title="Hermitage Amsterdam">Hermitage Museum</a> (right) on the <a href="/wiki/Amstel" title="Amstel">Amstel</a>.</center></div></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_area">Metropolitan area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Metropolitan area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Police_Headquarters,_Amsterdam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Police_Headquarters%2C_Amsterdam.jpg/220px-Police_Headquarters%2C_Amsterdam.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Police_Headquarters%2C_Amsterdam.jpg/330px-Police_Headquarters%2C_Amsterdam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Police_Headquarters%2C_Amsterdam.jpg/440px-Police_Headquarters%2C_Amsterdam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2056" data-file-height="3088" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Police_Headquarters,_Amsterdam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Police Headquarters of Amsterdam.</div></div></div>
<p>"Amsterdam" is usually understood to refer to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_of_the_Netherlands" title="List of municipalities of the Netherlands">municipality</a> of Amsterdam. Colloquially, some areas within the municipality, such as the town of <a href="/wiki/Durgerdam" title="Durgerdam">Durgerdam</a>, may not be considered part of Amsterdam.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Statistics_Netherlands" title="Statistics Netherlands">Statistics Netherlands</a> uses three other definitions of Amsterdam: metropolitan agglomeration Amsterdam (<i>Grootstedelijke Agglomeratie Amsterdam</i>, not to be confused with <i>Grootstedelijk Gebied Amsterdam</i>, a synonym of <i>Groot Amsterdam</i>), Greater Amsterdam (<i>Groot Amsterdam</i>, a <a href="/wiki/COROP" title="COROP">COROP</a> region) and the urban region Amsterdam (<i>Stadsgewest Amsterdam</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-cbs2013_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbs2013-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The Amsterdam Department for Research and Statistics uses a fourth conurbation, namely the <i>Stadsregio Amsterdam</i> ('City Region of Amsterdam'). The city region is similar to Greater Amsterdam but includes the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Zaanstad" title="Zaanstad">Zaanstad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wormerland" title="Wormerland">Wormerland</a>. It excludes <a href="/wiki/Graft-De_Rijp" title="Graft-De Rijp">Graft-De Rijp</a>.
</p><p>The smallest of these areas is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_of_the_Netherlands" title="List of municipalities of the Netherlands">municipality</a> of Amsterdam with a population of 802,938 in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-cbs2013_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbs2013-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The conurbation had a population of 1,096,042 in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-cbs2013_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbs2013-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> It includes the municipalities of Zaanstad, Wormerland, Oostzaan, Diemen and Amstelveen only, as well as the municipality of Amsterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-cbs2013_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbs2013-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Greater Amsterdam includes 15 municipalities,<sup id="cite_ref-cbs2013_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbs2013-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and had a population of 1,293,208 in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-cbs2013_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbs2013-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Though much larger in area, the population of this area is only slightly larger, because the definition excludes the relatively populous municipality of <a href="/wiki/Zaanstad" title="Zaanstad">Zaanstad</a>. The largest area by population, the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Metropolitan_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Metropolitan Area">Amsterdam Metropolitan Area</a> (Dutch: Metropoolregio Amsterdam), has a population of 2,33 million.<sup id="cite_ref-dosamsterdam_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dosamsterdam-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> It includes for instance Zaanstad, Wormerland, Muiden, Abcoude, Haarlem, Almere and Lelystad but excludes Graft-De Rijp. Amsterdam is part of the conglomerate metropolitan area <a href="/wiki/Randstad" title="Randstad">Randstad</a>, with a total population of 6,659,300 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-randstad_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-randstad-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Of these various metropolitan area configurations, only the <i>Stadsregio Amsterdam</i> (City Region of Amsterdam) has a formal governmental status. Its responsibities include regional spatial planning and the metropolitan public transport concessions.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_capital">National capital</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: National capital">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Capital_of_the_Netherlands" title="Capital of the Netherlands">Capital of the Netherlands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:King_Willem-Alexander,_Princess_Beatrix_en_Queen_Maxima.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/King_Willem-Alexander%2C_Princess_Beatrix_en_Queen_Maxima.jpg/220px-King_Willem-Alexander%2C_Princess_Beatrix_en_Queen_Maxima.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/King_Willem-Alexander%2C_Princess_Beatrix_en_Queen_Maxima.jpg/330px-King_Willem-Alexander%2C_Princess_Beatrix_en_Queen_Maxima.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/King_Willem-Alexander%2C_Princess_Beatrix_en_Queen_Maxima.jpg/440px-King_Willem-Alexander%2C_Princess_Beatrix_en_Queen_Maxima.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3996" data-file-height="2782" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:King_Willem-Alexander,_Princess_Beatrix_en_Queen_Maxima.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Willem-Alexander_of_the_Netherlands" title="Willem-Alexander of the Netherlands">King Willem-Alexander</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beatrix_of_the_Netherlands" title="Beatrix of the Netherlands">Princess Beatrix</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Queen_M%C3%A1xima_of_the_Netherlands" title="Queen Máxima of the Netherlands">Queen Máxima</a> greeting Amsterdammers from the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Palace_of_Amsterdam" title="Royal Palace of Amsterdam">Royal Palace of Amsterdam</a> during Willem-Alexanders inauguration in 2013.</div></div></div>
<p>Under the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Netherlands" title="Constitution of the Netherlands">Dutch Constitution</a>, Amsterdam is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_of_the_Netherlands" title="Capital of the Netherlands">capital of the Netherlands</a>. Since the 1983 constitutional revision, the constitution mentions "Amsterdam" and "capital" in chapter 2, article 32: The king's confirmation by oath and his coronation take place in "the capital Amsterdam" ("<i>de hoofdstad Amsterdam</i>").<sup id="cite_ref-capital-constitution_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-capital-constitution-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Previous versions of the constitution only mentioned "the city of Amsterdam" ("<i>de stad Amsterdam</i>").<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> For a royal investiture, therefore, the <a href="/wiki/States_General_of_the_Netherlands" title="States General of the Netherlands">States General of the Netherlands</a> (the Dutch Parliament) meets for a ceremonial joint session in Amsterdam. The ceremony traditionally takes place at the <a href="/wiki/Nieuwe_Kerk_(Amsterdam)" class="mw-redirect" title="Nieuwe Kerk (Amsterdam)">Nieuwe Kerk</a> on <a href="/wiki/Dam_Square" title="Dam Square">Dam Square</a>, immediately after the former monarch has signed the act of abdication at the nearby <a href="/wiki/Royal_Palace_of_Amsterdam" title="Royal Palace of Amsterdam">Royal Palace of Amsterdam</a>. Normally, however, the Parliament sits in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>, the city which has historically been the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Netherlands" title="Politics of the Netherlands">Dutch government</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Monarchy of the Netherlands">Dutch monarchy</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Netherlands" title="Supreme Court of the Netherlands">Dutch supreme court</a>. Foreign embassies are also located in The Hague.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Amsterdam" title="Coat of arms of Amsterdam">Coat of arms of Amsterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Amsterdam" title="Flag of Amsterdam">Flag of Amsterdam</a></div>
<p>The coat of arms of Amsterdam is composed of several historical elements. First and centre are three <a href="/wiki/Saltire" title="Saltire">St Andrew's crosses</a>, aligned in a vertical band on the city's shield (although Amsterdam's <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> was <a href="/wiki/Saint_Nicholas" title="Saint Nicholas">Saint Nicholas</a>). These St Andrew's crosses can also be found on the cityshields of neighbours <a href="/wiki/Amstelveen" title="Amstelveen">Amstelveen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ouder-Amstel" title="Ouder-Amstel">Ouder-Amstel</a>. This part of the coat of arms is the basis of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Amsterdam" title="Flag of Amsterdam">flag of Amsterdam</a>, flown by the city government, but also as <a href="/wiki/Civil_ensign" title="Civil ensign">civil ensign</a> for ships registered in Amsterdam. Second is the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Crown_of_Austria" title="Imperial Crown of Austria">Imperial Crown of Austria</a>. In 1489, out of gratitude for services and loans, <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Maximilian I, Holy Roman Emperor">Maximilian I</a> awarded Amsterdam the right to adorn its coat of arms with the <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Romans" title="King of the Romans">king's</a> crown. Then, in 1508, this was replaced with Maximilian's <a href="/wiki/Imperial_crown" title="Imperial crown">imperial crown</a> when he was crowned <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>. In the early years of the 17th century, Maximilian's crown in Amsterdam's coat of arms was again replaced, this time with the crown of <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Rudolf II, Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor Rudolph II</a>, a crown that became the Imperial <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Crown_Jewels" title="Austrian Crown Jewels">Crown of Austria</a>. The lions date from the late 16th century, when city and province became part of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Republic of the Seven United Netherlands</a>. Last came the city's official motto: <i>Heldhaftig, Vastberaden, Barmhartig</i> ("Heroic, Determined, Merciful"), bestowed on the city in 1947 by <a href="/wiki/Wilhelmina_of_the_Netherlands" title="Wilhelmina of the Netherlands">Queen Wilhelmina</a>, in recognition of the city's bravery during the Second World War.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Amsterdam" title="Transport in Amsterdam">Transport in Amsterdam</a></div>
<h3><span id="Metro.2C_tram_and_bus"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro,_tram_and_bus">Metro, tram and bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Metro, tram and bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Metro" title="Amsterdam Metro">Amsterdam Metro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Amsterdam" title="Trams in Amsterdam">Trams in Amsterdam</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_-_Keizersgracht_-_1316.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Amsterdam_-_Keizersgracht_-_1316.jpg/220px-Amsterdam_-_Keizersgracht_-_1316.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Amsterdam_-_Keizersgracht_-_1316.jpg/330px-Amsterdam_-_Keizersgracht_-_1316.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Amsterdam_-_Keizersgracht_-_1316.jpg/440px-Amsterdam_-_Keizersgracht_-_1316.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4368" data-file-height="2912" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_-_Keizersgracht_-_1316.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A tram crossing the Keizersgracht.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NoordZuidLijn_Metrostation_Europaplein_hnapel_004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/NoordZuidLijn_Metrostation_Europaplein_hnapel_004.jpg/220px-NoordZuidLijn_Metrostation_Europaplein_hnapel_004.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/NoordZuidLijn_Metrostation_Europaplein_hnapel_004.jpg/330px-NoordZuidLijn_Metrostation_Europaplein_hnapel_004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/NoordZuidLijn_Metrostation_Europaplein_hnapel_004.jpg/440px-NoordZuidLijn_Metrostation_Europaplein_hnapel_004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7360" data-file-height="4078" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NoordZuidLijn_Metrostation_Europaplein_hnapel_004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Metro" title="Amsterdam Metro">Amsterdam Metro</a> is a mixed subway and above ground <a href="/wiki/Rapid_Transit" class="mw-redirect" title="Rapid Transit">rapid transit system</a> consisting of five lines.</div></div></div>
<p>Currently, there are sixteen <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Amsterdam" title="Trams in Amsterdam">tram routes</a> and five <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Metro" title="Amsterdam Metro">metro routes</a>. All are operated by municipal public transport operator <a href="/wiki/Gemeentelijk_Vervoerbedrijf" title="Gemeentelijk Vervoerbedrijf">Gemeentelijk Vervoerbedrijf</a> (GVB), which also runs the city bus network.
</p><p>Four fare-free GVB ferries carry pedestrians and cyclists across the <a href="/wiki/IJ_(Amsterdam)" title="IJ (Amsterdam)">IJ lake</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Boroughs_of_Amsterdam" title="Boroughs of Amsterdam">borough</a> of <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam-Noord" title="Amsterdam-Noord">Amsterdam-Noord</a>, and two fare-charging ferries run east and west along the harbour. There are also privately operated water taxis, a water bus, a <a href="/wiki/Boat_sharing" title="Boat sharing">boat sharing</a> operation, electric rental boats and canal cruises, that transport people along Amsterdam's waterways.
</p><p>Regional buses, and some suburban buses, are operated by <a href="/wiki/Connexxion" title="Connexxion">Connexxion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Egged_(company)" title="Egged (company)">EBS</a>. International coach services are provided by <a href="/wiki/Eurolines" title="Eurolines">Eurolines</a> from <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Amstel_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Amstel railway station">Amsterdam Amstel railway station</a>, <a href="/wiki/IDBUS" class="mw-redirect" title="IDBUS">IDBUS</a> from <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Sloterdijk_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Sloterdijk railway station">Amsterdam Sloterdijk railway station</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Megabus_(Europe)" title="Megabus (Europe)">Megabus</a> from the Zuiderzeeweg in the east of the city.
</p><p>In order to facilitate easier transport to the center of Amsterdam, the city has various P+R Locations where people can park their car at an affordable price and transfer to one of the numerous public transport lines.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Car">Car</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Car">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Amsterdam was intended in 1932 to be the hub, a kind of <a href="/wiki/Kilometre_Zero" class="mw-redirect" title="Kilometre Zero">Kilometre Zero</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_motorways_in_the_Netherlands" title="List of motorways in the Netherlands">highway system of the Netherlands</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Autosnelweg_1930_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Autosnelweg_1930-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> with freeways numbered One to Eight planned to originate from the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Autosnelweg_1930_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Autosnelweg_1930-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> The outbreak of the Second World War and shifting priorities led to the current situation, where only roads <a href="/wiki/A1_motorway_(Netherlands)" title="A1 motorway (Netherlands)">A1</a>, <a href="/wiki/A2_motorway_(Netherlands)" title="A2 motorway (Netherlands)">A2</a>, and <a href="/wiki/A4_motorway_(Netherlands)" title="A4 motorway (Netherlands)">A4</a> originate from Amsterdam according to the original plan. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=A3_motorway_(Netherlands)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="A3 motorway (Netherlands) (page does not exist)">A3</a> to <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> was cancelled in 1970 in order to conserve the <a href="/wiki/Groene_Hart" title="Groene Hart">Groene Hart</a>. Road <a href="/wiki/A8_motorway_(Netherlands)" title="A8 motorway (Netherlands)">A8</a>, leading north to <a href="/wiki/Zaandam" title="Zaandam">Zaandam</a> and the <a href="/wiki/A10_motorway_(Netherlands)" title="A10 motorway (Netherlands)">A10</a> <a href="/wiki/Beltway" class="mw-redirect" title="Beltway">Ringroad</a> were opened between 1968 and 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-Autosnelweg_1970_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Autosnelweg_1970-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> Besides the A1, A2, A4 and A8, several freeways, such as the <a href="/wiki/A7_motorway_(Netherlands)" title="A7 motorway (Netherlands)">A7</a> and <a href="/wiki/A6_motorway_(Netherlands)" title="A6 motorway (Netherlands)">A6</a>, carry traffic mainly bound for Amsterdam.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/A10_motorway_(Netherlands)" title="A10 motorway (Netherlands)">A10 ringroad</a> surrounding the city connects Amsterdam with the Dutch <a href="/wiki/List_of_motorways_in_the_Netherlands" title="List of motorways in the Netherlands">national network of freeways</a>. <a href="/wiki/Interchange_(road)" title="Interchange (road)">Interchanges</a> on the A10 allow cars to enter the city by transferring to one of the 18 <i>city roads</i>, numbered S101 through to S118. These city roads are regional roads without <a href="/wiki/Grade_separation" title="Grade separation">grade separation</a>, and sometimes without a <a href="/wiki/Central_reservation" class="mw-redirect" title="Central reservation">central reservation</a>. Most are accessible by cyclists. The S100 <i>Centrumring</i> is a smaller ringroad circumnavigating the city's centre.
</p><p>In the city centre, driving a car is discouraged. Parking fees are expensive, and many streets are closed to cars or are <a href="/wiki/One-way_traffic" title="One-way traffic">one-way</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fiets_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fiets-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> The local government sponsors <a href="/wiki/Carsharing" title="Carsharing">carsharing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carpool" title="Carpool">carpooling</a> initiatives such as <i>Autodelen</i> and <i>Meerijden.nu</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-cars_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cars-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_rail">National rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: National rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Central_Station1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Amsterdam_Central_Station1.jpg/250px-Amsterdam_Central_Station1.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Amsterdam_Central_Station1.jpg/375px-Amsterdam_Central_Station1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Amsterdam_Central_Station1.jpg/500px-Amsterdam_Central_Station1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4872" data-file-height="2051" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_Central_Station1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Centraal_station" title="Amsterdam Centraal station">Amsterdam Centraal station</a>, the city's main train station.</div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam is served by ten <a href="/wiki/Railway_stations_in_the_Netherlands#A" title="Railway stations in the Netherlands">stations</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Nederlandse_Spoorwegen" title="Nederlandse Spoorwegen">Nederlandse Spoorwegen</a> (Dutch Railways).<sup id="cite_ref-Stationsweb_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stationsweb-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> Five are intercity stops: <a href="/wiki/Sloterdijk_(Amsterdam)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sloterdijk (Amsterdam)">Sloterdijk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Zuid_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Zuid railway station">Zuid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Amstel_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Amstel railway station">Amstel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Bijlmer_ArenA_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Bijlmer ArenA railway station">Bijlmer ArenA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Centraal_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Centraal railway station">Amsterdam Centraal</a>. The stations for local services are: <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Lelylaan_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Lelylaan railway station">Lelylaan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_RAI_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam RAI railway station">RAI</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Holendrecht_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Holendrecht railway station">Holendrecht</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Muiderpoort_railway_station" title="Amsterdam Muiderpoort railway station">Muiderpoort</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Science_Park_railway_station" title="Amsterdam Science Park railway station">Science Park</a>. <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Centraal_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Centraal railway station">Amsterdam Centraal</a> is also an international railway station. From the station there are regular services to destinations such as Austria, Belarus, Belgium, the Czech Republic, Denmark, France, Germany, Hungary, Poland, Russia, Switzerland and the United Kingdom. Among these trains are international trains of the <a href="/wiki/Nederlandse_Spoorwegen" title="Nederlandse Spoorwegen">Nederlandse Spoorwegen</a> (Amsterdam-Berlin), the <a href="/wiki/Eurostar" title="Eurostar">Eurostar</a> (Amsterdam-Brussels-London), <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">Thalys</a> (Amsterdam-Brussels-Paris/Lille), and <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">Intercity-Express</a> (Amsterdam–Cologne–Frankfurt).<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport">Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schiphol_Airport_Pier_D_(7325966610).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Schiphol_Airport_Pier_D_%287325966610%29.jpg/220px-Schiphol_Airport_Pier_D_%287325966610%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Schiphol_Airport_Pier_D_%287325966610%29.jpg/330px-Schiphol_Airport_Pier_D_%287325966610%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Schiphol_Airport_Pier_D_%287325966610%29.jpg/440px-Schiphol_Airport_Pier_D_%287325966610%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4250" data-file-height="2834" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schiphol_Airport_Pier_D_(7325966610).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Amsterdam Airport Schiphol</a> ranks as Europe's third-busiest airport for passenger traffic.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Amsterdam Airport Schiphol</a> is less than 20 minutes by train from <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Centraal_station" title="Amsterdam Centraal station">Amsterdam Centraal station</a> and is served by domestic and international intercity trains, such as <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">Thalys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurostar" title="Eurostar">Eurostar</a> and Intercity Brussel. Schiphol is the largest airport in the Netherlands, the third largest in Europe, and the 14th-largest in the world in terms of passengers. It handles over 68 million passengers per year and is the home base of four airlines, <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transavia" title="Transavia">Transavia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martinair" title="Martinair">Martinair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arkefly" class="mw-redirect" title="Arkefly">Arkefly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Schiphol was the fifth <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_international_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s busiest airports by international passenger traffic">busiest airport in the world</a> measured by international passenger numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-passengerrank_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-passengerrank-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> This airport is 4 meters below sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cycling">Cycling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Cycling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cycling_in_Amsterdam" title="Cycling in Amsterdam">Cycling in Amsterdam</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_-_Bicycles_-_1058.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Amsterdam_-_Bicycles_-_1058.jpg/220px-Amsterdam_-_Bicycles_-_1058.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Amsterdam_-_Bicycles_-_1058.jpg/330px-Amsterdam_-_Bicycles_-_1058.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Amsterdam_-_Bicycles_-_1058.jpg/440px-Amsterdam_-_Bicycles_-_1058.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4368" data-file-height="2912" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amsterdam_-_Bicycles_-_1058.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Police bicyclist crossing a bridge over the Prinsengracht.</div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam is one of the most bicycle-friendly large cities in the world and is a centre of <a href="/wiki/Bicycle_culture" title="Bicycle culture">bicycle culture</a> with good facilities for cyclists such as bike paths and <a href="/wiki/Bicycle_stand" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicycle stand">bike racks</a>, and several guarded bike storage garages (<i>fietsenstalling</i>) which can be used.
</p><p>In 2013, there were about 1,200,000 bicycles in Amsterdam outnumbering the number of citizens in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> Theft is widespread—in 2011, about 83,000 bicycles were stolen in Amsterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> Bicycles are used by all socio-economic groups because of their convenience, Amsterdam's small size, the 400 kilometres (249 miles) of bike paths,<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> the flat terrain, and the inconvenience of driving an automobile.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Agnietenkapel_Gate.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Agnietenkapel_Gate.jpg/220px-Agnietenkapel_Gate.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Agnietenkapel_Gate.jpg/330px-Agnietenkapel_Gate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Agnietenkapel_Gate.jpg/440px-Agnietenkapel_Gate.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Agnietenkapel_Gate.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Agnietenkapel Gate at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Amsterdam" title="University of Amsterdam">University of Amsterdam</a>, founded in 1632 as the Athenaeum Illustre.</div></div></div>
<p>Amsterdam has two universities: the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Amsterdam" title="University of Amsterdam">University of Amsterdam</a> (<i>Universiteit van Amsterdam</i>, UvA), and the <i><a href="/wiki/Vrije_Universiteit_Amsterdam" title="Vrije Universiteit Amsterdam">Vrije Universiteit Amsterdam</a></i> (VU).
