Other institutions for higher education include an <a href="/wiki/Art_school" title="Art school">art school</a> – <a href="/wiki/Gerrit_Rietveld_Academie" title="Gerrit Rietveld Academie">Gerrit Rietveld Academie</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Hogeschool" class="mw-redirect" title="Hogeschool">university of applied sciences</a> – the <a href="/wiki/Hogeschool_van_Amsterdam" title="Hogeschool van Amsterdam">Hogeschool van Amsterdam</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdamse_Hogeschool_voor_de_Kunsten" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdamse Hogeschool voor de Kunsten">Amsterdamse Hogeschool voor de Kunsten</a>. Amsterdam's <a href="/wiki/International_Institute_of_Social_History" title="International Institute of Social History">International Institute of Social History</a> is one of the world's largest documentary and research institutions concerning <a href="/wiki/Social_history" title="Social history">social history</a>, and especially the <a href="/wiki/Labor_history_(discipline)" title="Labor history (discipline)">history of the labour movement</a>. Amsterdam's <a href="/wiki/Hortus_Botanicus_(Amsterdam)" title="Hortus Botanicus (Amsterdam)">Hortus Botanicus</a>, founded in the early 17th century, is one of the oldest botanical gardens in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-Hortus_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hortus-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> with many old and rare specimens, among them the <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee plant</a> that served as the parent for the entire <a href="/wiki/Coffee_culture" title="Coffee culture">coffee culture</a> in Central and South America.<sup id="cite_ref-he_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-he-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are over 200 primary schools in Amsterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> Some of these primary schools base their teachings on particular pedagogic theories like the various <a href="/wiki/Maria_Montessori" title="Maria Montessori">Montessori</a> schools. The biggest Montessori high school in Amsterdam is the <a href="/wiki/Montessori_Lyceum_Amsterdam" title="Montessori Lyceum Amsterdam">Montessori Lyceum Amsterdam</a>. Many schools, however, are based on religion. This used to be primarily Roman Catholicism and various Protestant denominations, but with the influx of Muslim immigrants there has been a rise in the number of Islamic schools. Jewish schools can be found in the southern suburbs of Amsterdam.
</p><p>Amsterdam is noted for having five independent grammar schools (Dutch: gymnasia), the <a href="/wiki/Vossius_Gymnasium" title="Vossius Gymnasium">Vossius Gymnasium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barlaeus_Gymnasium" title="Barlaeus Gymnasium">Barlaeus Gymnasium</a>, St. <a href="/wiki/Ignatius_Gymnasium" title="Ignatius Gymnasium">Ignatius Gymnasium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Het_4e_Gymnasium" title="Het 4e Gymnasium">Het 4e Gymnasium</a> and the Cygnus Gymnasium where a classical curriculum including <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">classical Greek</a> is taught. Though believed until recently by many to be an anachronistic and elitist concept that would soon die out, the gymnasia have recently experienced a revival, leading to the formation of a fourth and fifth grammar school in which the three aforementioned schools participate. Most secondary schools in Amsterdam offer a variety of different levels of education in the same school. The city also has various colleges ranging from art and design to politics and economics which are mostly also available for students coming from other countries.
</p><p>Schools for foreign nationals in Amsterdam include the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_International_Community_School" title="Amsterdam International Community School">Amsterdam International Community School</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_School_of_Amsterdam" title="British School of Amsterdam">British School of Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein_International_School_Amsterdam" title="Albert Einstein International School Amsterdam">Albert Einstein International School Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyc%C3%A9e_Vincent_van_Gogh_La_Haye-Amsterdam" title="Lycée Vincent van Gogh La Haye-Amsterdam">Lycée Vincent van Gogh La Haye-Amsterdam</a> primary campus (French school), <a href="/wiki/International_School_of_Amsterdam" class="mw-redirect" title="International School of Amsterdam">International School of Amsterdam</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_School_of_Amsterdam" title="Japanese School of Amsterdam">Japanese School of Amsterdam</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Amsterdam" title="List of people from Amsterdam">List of people from Amsterdam</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Amsterdam is a prominent centre for national and international media. Some locally based newspapers include <i><a href="/wiki/Het_Parool" title="Het Parool">Het Parool</a></i>, a national daily paper; <i><a href="/wiki/De_Telegraaf" title="De Telegraaf">De Telegraaf</a></i>, the largest Dutch daily newspaper; the daily newspapers <i><a href="/wiki/Trouw" title="Trouw">Trouw</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/De_Volkskrant" title="De Volkskrant">de Volkskrant</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/NRC_Handelsblad" title="NRC Handelsblad">NRC Handelsblad</a></i>; <i><a href="/wiki/De_Groene_Amsterdammer" title="De Groene Amsterdammer">De Groene Amsterdammer</a></i>, a weekly newspaper; the free newspapers <i><a href="/wiki/Sp!ts" class="mw-redirect" title="Sp!ts">Sp!ts</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Metro_(Dutch_newspaper)" title="Metro (Dutch newspaper)">Metro</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Holland_Times" title="The Holland Times">The Holland Times</a></i> (printed in English).
</p><p>Amsterdam is home to the second-largest Dutch commercial TV group <a href="/wiki/SBS_Broadcasting_Group" title="SBS Broadcasting Group">SBS Broadcasting Group</a>, consisting of TV-stations <a href="/wiki/SBS_6" class="mw-redirect" title="SBS 6">SBS 6</a>, <a href="/wiki/Net_5" class="mw-redirect" title="Net 5">Net 5</a> and <a href="/wiki/Veronica_(TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Veronica (TV channel)">Veronica</a>. However, Amsterdam is not considered 'the media city of the Netherlands'. The town of <a href="/wiki/Hilversum" title="Hilversum">Hilversum</a>, 30 kilometres (19 miles) south-east of Amsterdam, has been crowned with this unofficial title. Hilversum is the principal centre for radio and television broadcasting in the Netherlands. <a href="/wiki/Radio_Netherlands_Worldwide" title="Radio Netherlands Worldwide">Radio Netherlands</a>, heard worldwide via shortwave radio since the 1920s, is also based there. Hilversum is home to an extensive complex of audio and television studios belonging to the national broadcast production company NOS, as well as to the studios and offices of all the Dutch public broadcasting organisations and many commercial TV production companies.
</p><p>In 2012, the music video of Far East Movement, 'Live My Life', was filmed in various parts of Amsterdam.
</p><p>Also, several movies were filmed in Amsterdam, such as <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Diamonds_Are_Forever_(film)" title="Diamonds Are Forever (film)">Diamonds Are Forever</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ocean%27s_Twelve" title="Ocean&#39;s Twelve">Ocean's Twelve</a>, <a href="/wiki/Girl_with_a_Pearl_Earring_(film)" title="Girl with a Pearl Earring (film)">Girl with a Pearl Earring</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Hitman%27s_Bodyguard" title="The Hitman&#39;s Bodyguard">The Hitman's Bodyguard</a>. Amsterdam is also featured in <a href="/wiki/John_Green_(author)" title="John Green (author)">John Green</a>'s book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars">The Fault in Our Stars</a></i>, which has been made into <a href="/wiki/The_Fault_in_Our_Stars_(film)" title="The Fault in Our Stars (film)">a film</a> as well that partly takes place in Amsterdam.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amsterdam&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The housing market is heavily regulated. In Amsterdam, 55% of existing housing and 30% of new housing is owned by Housing Associations, which are Government sponsored entities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="stat needs ref (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>From the late 1960s onwards many buildings in Amsterdam have been <a href="/wiki/Squatting" title="Squatting">squatted</a> both for housing and for using as social centres.<sup id="cite_ref-Owens_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Owens-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> A number of these squats have legalised and become well known, such as <a href="/wiki/OCCII" title="OCCII">OCCII</a>, <a href="/wiki/OT301" title="OT301">OT301</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paradiso_(Amsterdam)" title="Paradiso (Amsterdam)">Paradiso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vrankrijk" title="Vrankrijk">Vrankrijk</a>.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">After Athens in 1888 and Florence in 1986, Amsterdam was in 1986 chosen as the <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a>, confirming its eminent position in Europe and the Netherlands. <li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Case in point: After <a href="/wiki/Galileo_affair" title="Galileo affair">his trial and sentencing</a> in Rome in 1633, <a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">Galileo</a> chose <a href="/wiki/Lodewijk_Elzevir" title="Lodewijk Elzevir">Lodewijk Elzevir</a> in Amsterdam to publish one of his finest works, <i><a href="/wiki/Two_New_Sciences" title="Two New Sciences">Two New Sciences</a></i>. See Wade Rowland (2003), <i>Galileo's Mistake, A new look at the epic confrontation between Galileo and the Church</i>, New York: <a href="/wiki/Arcade_Publishing" title="Arcade Publishing">Arcade Publishing</a>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-55970-684-8" title="Special:BookSources/1-55970-684-8">1-55970-684-8</a>, p. 260.</span>
